Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
8 min
Invalidity of Sale with Uncertain Deferred Term
Explanation of the ruling that a sale deferred to an uncertain time is invalid due to ignorance of the term.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a sale with deferred payment to an uncertain time and explain the legal cause (illa) behind its invalidity.

Core Idea
A sale deferred to an uncertain future event is fasid because ignorance of the term leads to unavoidable dispute.

This lesson examines a classic Hanafi ruling on sales where the payment term is tied to an event like Nowruz or the Christian fast. The key is jahalah (ignorance) of the term, which makes the contract invalid even if the parties agree. We will explore why the Hanafi school considers this fatal and how the ruling applies when both parties actually know the term.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
The passage states that selling with deferment to Nowruz, Mihrajan, Christian fast, or Jewish break-fast is not permissible and the sale is fasid (invalid). That is the core ruling.
The ruling applies to any uncertain future event, not just these four.
2
Locate the Legal Cause (Illa)
The text explicitly gives the cause: 'لجهالة الأجل وهي مفضية إلى المنازعة' – because of ignorance of the term, which leads to dispute. The cause is jahalah, and the underlying reason is that sales are based on mutual bargaining (mumakasah), so certainty is essential.
This is a talil (reasoning) based on public interest.
3
Trace the Dalil
The dalil here is not a direct text from Quran or Sunnah but istihsan (juristic preference) based on the maqsad of avoiding dispute. The Hanafi school uses the maxim that the ruling revolves with its cause.
Istihsan is a valid source in Hanafi usul.
4
Apply the Criterion: Knowledge of the Term
The sale becomes valid if both parties know the term exactly. For example, if they know Nowruz as the first day of spring astronomically, the sale is valid. The text also notes that the Christian break-fast (Easter) is known by calculation, so it is valid.
The criterion is knowledge, not the nature of the event itself.

البيع إلى النيروز والمهرجان وصوم النصارى وفطر اليهود إن لم يدر العاقدان ذلك وإلى قدوم القبقاب كتشريك النعل كما في فتح القدير. وفي البزازية : اشترى ثوباً أو خفاً خلقاً على أن يرقعه البائع ويخرزه ويسلمه صح للعرف ومعنى يحذوه يقطعه قوله : (لا البيع إلى النيروز والمهرجان وصوم النصارى وفطر اليهود إن لم يدر العاقدان (ذلك أي لا يجوز البيع وهو فاسد لجهالة الأجل وهي مفضية إلى المنازعة في البيع لابتنائها على المماكسة إلا إذا كانا يعرفانه لكونه معلوماً عندهما أو كان التأجيل إلى فطر النصارى بعدما شرعوا في صومهم بالأيام لأن صومهم بالأيام معلوم فلا جهالة فيه والنيروز أول يوم من الصيف وهو أول يوم تحل فيه الشمس الحمل. والمهرجان أول يوم من الشتاء وهو أول يوم تحل فيه الشمس الميزان؛ كذا في السراج الوهاج . ثم قال : وإنما خص الصوم بالنصارى والفطر باليهود لأن غير معلوم وفطرهم معلوم واليهود بعكسه مع أنه إذا باع إلى صوم اليهود فالحكم كذلك لا

قوله : (وقدمنا أنه لو باع الخ قال الرملي : قدم أنه يفتي بأنه يتأجل إلى شهر قال : كأنه لأنه
Book of Sale, Chapter of Invalid Sale. Selling with deferment to Nowruz, Mihrajan, the fast of Christians, and the break-fast of Jews, if the two contracting parties do not know that, and to the arrival of the sandal... as in Fath al-Qadir. In al-Bazzaziyya: He bought a garment or old shoe on condition that the seller patches it, sews it, and delivers it—valid due to custom, and the meaning of 'yahdhuhu' is he cuts it. He said: 'Do not sell to Nowruz, Mihrajan, the fast of Christians, and the break-fast of Jews if the two contracting parties do not know that'—that is, the sale is not permissible and it is invalid due to ignorance of the term, which leads to dispute in sale because it is based on haggling, unless they both know it because it is known to them, or the deferment is to the break-fast of Christians after they have begun their fast with days, because their fast is known by days so there is no ignorance. Nowruz is the first day of summer, and it is the first day the sun enters Aries. Mihrajan is the first day of winter, and it is the first day the sun enters Libra; thus in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. Then he said: He specified the fast with Christians and the break-fast with Jews because [the fast of Christians] is unknown and their break-fast is known, and the opposite for Jews; if he sells with deferment to the fast of Jews, the ruling is likewise not... winter is based on the fast of Christians. If one of them knows and the other does not, likewise it is not permissible because it leads to dispute. The expression of al-Islah by Ibn Kamal Pasha: if one of them does not know that... end. The expression free from criticism: if they both do not know or one of them, reflect. His saying: 'Nowruz is the first day of summer etc.' He said in al-Nahr: This is only complete based on spring being part of summer and autumn part of winter, and its like has passed in the chapter of prayer, otherwise the seasons are four, as is not hidden. And it is said: They are two festivals of the Magians... end. He mentioned before: Nowruz is the first day of spring when the sun enters Aries, and Mihrajan is a day in autumn, the first day of winter when the sun enters Libra... end. And it is not hidden that his saying 'it is the first day of' that autumn is from winter, otherwise the first season of winter is the day the sun enters Capricorn; if he dropped it, it would be better, reflect. In al-Qahistani: Nowruz has types: common Nowruz is the first day of Farvardin month; special Nowruz is the special Nowruz; the Sultan's Nowruz is the first day when at noon the sun is in the first degree of Aries; the Magians' Nowruz, also called the Dehqans' Nowruz, is the day the sun enters Pisces. Mihrajan has two types: common is the first day of autumn, that is, the sixteenth of Mehr month; special is the twenty-sixth of it... end. His saying: 'Then he said etc.' Al-Ramli said: It is not hidden to one of understanding that his saying in the matn 'if the two contracting parties do not know that' following what is in other works, that the criterion is the knowledge of the contracting parties alone because the ignorance is taken as the cause of invalidity, and the ruling revolves with it however it revolves, so Nowruz, Mihrajan, Christian fast and their break-fast, Jewish break-fast and their fast must be equal in that—reflect. Because with his saying... His saying: 'Though if he sells with deferment to the fast of Jews, the ruling is likewise'—that is, if they know it, it is valid, otherwise not; and reflect: the Christian fast is unknown, etc. In al-Qahistani: The Christian fast is thirty-seven days within a period of forty-eight days; their fast begins on Monday near the conjunction of the two lights occurring on the second of February and the eighth of March; they do not fast Sunday or Saturday except the forty-eighth Saturday; their break-fast, meaning their feast day, is the Sunday after that. The Jewish break-fast is that they eat for seven days from the fifteenth of the seventh month of their calendar, beginning before the Roman year by a month, corresponding to Moses and his people. As for the Jewish break-fast, as in al-Hidayah and others, it is not a famous day among them, unless it is said that it means the day they break their fast, for they fast by the text of the Torah for thirty-six days... end. The author's saying: 'al-Diyas'—al-Ramli said, al-Mutarrizi said: al-Diyasah in food is that it is trodden by the feet of beasts and repeated treading means until it becomes straw. Al-Diyas is polishing the sword, and the jurists' use of it in the place of al-Diyasah is either laxity or a mistake... end. His saying: 'Muhammad ibn al-Fadl said: it invalidates the sale.' We previously mentioned at the author's saying in the Book of Sales: 'and valid with an immediate price and a known term' from al-Khaniyya that the invalidity is the saying of Abu Hanifa and that it is correct. In Ghayat al-Bayan, Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi said: If it is said that slight ignorance is tolerated in one place does not indicate that deferment to these unknown times is tolerated; do you not see that the dower tolerates slight ignorance as it tolerates ignorance of description, yet stipulating these terms is not valid in it... end. Then he said: The answer to this section is not preserved in the books, and among our teachers there is difference of opinion on it; the most correct is that these terms are established in the dower because there is no doubt that stipulating these terms does not affect the original marriage contract, unlike sale, so this remains a defect in the debt established by the contract. His saying: 'And we previously mentioned that if he sells etc.' Al-Ramli said: He previously mentioned that he gives fatwa that it is deferred until a month; he said: as if because

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq is a commentary on the matn of Kanz al-Daqaiq in the chapter of invalid sales. The core ruling is that a sale with a deferred payment tied to an uncertain future event—such as Nowruz, Mihrajan, the Christian fast, or the Jewish break-fast—is invalid (fasid) if the term is not known to both parties at the time of contract. The reason given is 'jahalah al-ajal' (ignorance of the term), which leads to dispute (munaza'ah) because sale transactions are based on mutual agreement and bargaining (mumakasah). If both parties know the term, the sale is valid. The author then clarifies the definitions of Nowruz and Mihrajan based on astronomical positions (sun entering Aries for Nowruz, Libra for Mihrajan), noting that these are seasonal markers. He also distinguishes between the Christian fast (which is unknown by days because it's a movable fast) and their break-fast (Easter, which is known by days), and similarly for Jews. The commentary expands to include other uncertain times like the arrival of pilgrims, harvest, threshing, and vintage—all invalid due to variability. A key nuance: if the deferment is made after the contract is valid (e.g., by subsequent agreement), it may be permissible according to some scholars, but the original stipulation in the contract causes invalidity. The passage also discusses surety (kafala) with such terms, which is valid because slight ignorance is tolerated in surety. Finally, there is an intra-madhhab dispute: Muhammad ibn al-Fadl says postponement after a valid contract invalidates the sale, while Muhammad al-Shaybani says it is valid as a voluntary deferment. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that the invalidity is the statement of Abu Hanifa and it is correct. The text emphasizes that the criterion is the knowledge of both parties; if only one knows, the sale is still invalid.

Key Terms
النيروز (al-Nayruz): Nowruz, the first day of spring/summer when the sun enters Aries; a Persian festival.
المهرجان (al-Mihrajan): Mihrajan, the first day of autumn/winter when the sun enters Libra; another Persian festival.
الجهالة (al-Jahalah): Ignorance or uncertainty regarding a contractual term, leading to invalidity in sales.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary reason a sale with deferment to Nowruz is considered invalid (fasid) according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because Nowruz is a pagan festival
B) Because the term is unknown (jahalah) which leads to dispute
C) Because it is a sale of a non-existent object
D) Because the price is not specified

Key Takeaway
A sale with a deferred payment to an uncertain future event is fasid because jahalah leads to dispute; it becomes valid only if both parties know the term.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

Knowledge of Both Parties and Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Expansion on the condition of knowledge and an intra-Hanafi dispute about the effect of subsequent deferment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi condition that both contracting parties must know the deferred term, and distinguish between the views of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad ibn al-Fadl on whether a subsequent agreement can validate the sale.

Core Idea
One party's knowledge is insufficient; both must know, and a later agreement does not cure the initial invalidity according to the relied-upon view.

The previous lesson established that ignorance of the term invalidates the sale. But what if only one party knows? And what if they later agree on a known term? This lesson dives into the details: the Hanafi position that both must know, and an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether a post-contract deferment can rescue the sale.

Guided Path
1
Confirm the Condition: Both Parties Must Know
The text states: 'لا البيع إلى ... إن لم يدر العاقدان ذلك' and later clarifies that if one knows and the other does not, the sale is still invalid because it leads to dispute. So the condition is joint knowledge.
This is a stricter condition than some other contracts.
2
Analyze the Exception: When the Event is Known
The text notes that deferment to the Christian break-fast (Easter) is valid because it is a known day. Similarly, if the deferment is to a specific known event like 'harvest time' if harvest dates are known, it may be valid.
The ruling depends on whether the event is fixed or variable.
3
Identify the Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf
Muhammad ibn al-Fadl says that if the sale is initially valid (e.g., with a known price) and then the parties agree to defer payment to an uncertain time, the sale becomes invalid. But Muhammad al-Shaybani says it is valid as a voluntary deferment. The relied-upon view (mufta bihi) is Abu Hanifa's position that it becomes invalid.
This shows that even a subsequent agreement cannot cure the initial defect.
4
Determine the Practical Application
In practice, if a sale is made with a deferred term that is unknown to one party, the sale is fasid. The parties must either cancel and re-contract with a known term, or if the term later becomes known, some scholars validate it, but the cautious approach is to re-contract.
The principle is to avoid any potential dispute.

قوله : (مع أنه إذا باع إلى صوم اليهود فالحكم كذلك أي أن علماه صح وإلا فلا وتأمله صوم النصارى غير معلوم «الخ. وفي القهستاني : وصوم النصارى سبعة وثلاثون يوماً في مدة ثمانية وأربعين يوماً فإن ابتداء صومهم يوم الاثنين الذي يكون قريباً من اجتماع النيرين الواقع ثاني شباط وثامن آذار ولا يصومون يوم الأحد ولا يوم السبت إلا يوم السبت الثامن والأربعين، ويكون فطرهم يعني يوم عيدهم يوم الأحد بعد ذلك. وفطر اليهود أن يأكلوا سبعة أيام من خامس عشر من الشهر السابع من شهر تاريخهم ابتداؤه قبل سنة الروم بشهر الموافقة موسى وقومه، وأما فطر اليهود كما في الهداية وغيرها فليس بيوم مشهور عنهم إلا أن يقال أريد يوم أفطروا فيه فإنهم يصومون بنص التوراة ستة وثلاثين يوماً .اهـ. قول المصنف : (والدياس) قال الرملي قال المطرزي : الدياسة في الطعام أن يوطأ بقوائم الدواب ويكرر عليه الدوس يعني الجرجر حتى يصير تبناً. والدياس صقل السيف واستعمال الفقهاء إياه في موضع الدياسة تسامح أو وهم .اهـ. قوله (قال محمد بن الفضل يفسد البيع) قدمنا عند قول المصنف في كتاب البيوع وصح) بثمن حال وبأجل معلوم» عن الخانية أيضاً أن الفساد قول أبي حنيفة وأنه الصحيح. وفي غاية البيان وقال شمس الأئمة السرخسي : فإن قيل كون الجهالة اليسيرة متحملة في موضع لا يدل على أن يكون التأجيل إلى هذه الأوقات المجهولة متحملاً ألا ترى أن الصداق يتحمل الجهالة اليسيرة حيث يتحمل جهالة الوصف ثم لا يصح فيه اشتراط هذه الآجال .اهـ. ثم قال: جواب هذا الفصل غير محفوظ في الكتب وبين مشايخنا فيه اختلاف، والأصح أنه تثبت هذه الآجال في الصداق لأنه لا شك أن اشتراط هذه الآجال لا تؤثر في أصل النكاح بخلاف البيع فيبقى هذا خللاً في الدين المستحق بالعقد.
قوله : (وقدمنا أنه لو باع الخ قال الرملي : قدم أنه يفتي بأنه يتأجل إلى شهر قال : كأنه لأنه
Book of Sale, Chapter of Invalid Sale. Selling with deferment to Nowruz, Mihrajan, the fast of Christians, and the break-fast of Jews, if the two contracting parties do not know that, and to the arrival of the sandal... as in Fath al-Qadir. In al-Bazzaziyya: He bought a garment or old shoe on condition that the seller patches it, sews it, and delivers it—valid due to custom, and the meaning of 'yahdhuhu' is he cuts it. He said: 'Do not sell to Nowruz, Mihrajan, the fast of Christians, and the break-fast of Jews if the two contracting parties do not know that'—that is, the sale is not permissible and it is invalid due to ignorance of the term, which leads to dispute in sale because it is based on haggling, unless they both know it because it is known to them, or the deferment is to the break-fast of Christians after they have begun their fast with days, because their fast is known by days so there is no ignorance. Nowruz is the first day of summer, and it is the first day the sun enters Aries. Mihrajan is the first day of winter, and it is the first day the sun enters Libra; thus in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. Then he said: He specified the fast with Christians and the break-fast with Jews because [the fast of Christians] is unknown and their break-fast is known, and the opposite for Jews; if he sells with deferment to the fast of Jews, the ruling is likewise not... winter is based on the fast of Christians. If one of them knows and the other does not, likewise it is not permissible because it leads to dispute. The expression of al-Islah by Ibn Kamal Pasha: if one of them does not know that... end. The expression free from criticism: if they both do not know or one of them, reflect. His saying: 'Nowruz is the first day of summer etc.' He said in al-Nahr: This is only complete based on spring being part of summer and autumn part of winter, and its like has passed in the chapter of prayer, otherwise the seasons are four, as is not hidden. And it is said: They are two festivals of the Magians... end. He mentioned before: Nowruz is the first day of spring when the sun enters Aries, and Mihrajan is a day in autumn, the first day of winter when the sun enters Libra... end. And it is not hidden that his saying 'it is the first day of' that autumn is from winter, otherwise the first season of winter is the day the sun enters Capricorn; if he dropped it, it would be better, reflect. In al-Qahistani: Nowruz has types: common Nowruz is the first day of Farvardin month; special Nowruz is the special Nowruz; the Sultan's Nowruz is the first day when at noon the sun is in the first degree of Aries; the Magians' Nowruz, also called the Dehqans' Nowruz, is the day the sun enters Pisces. Mihrajan has two types: common is the first day of autumn, that is, the sixteenth of Mehr month; special is the twenty-sixth of it... end. His saying: 'Then he said etc.' Al-Ramli said: It is not hidden to one of understanding that his saying in the matn 'if the two contracting parties do not know that' following what is in other works, that the criterion is the knowledge of the contracting parties alone because the ignorance is taken as the cause of invalidity, and the ruling revolves with it however it revolves, so Nowruz, Mihrajan, Christian fast and their break-fast, Jewish break-fast and their fast must be equal in that—reflect. Because with his saying... His saying: 'Though if he sells with deferment to the fast of Jews, the ruling is likewise'—that is, if they know it, it is valid, otherwise not; and reflect: the Christian fast is unknown, etc. In al-Qahistani: The Christian fast is thirty-seven days within a period of forty-eight days; their fast begins on Monday near the conjunction of the two lights occurring on the second of February and the eighth of March; they do not fast Sunday or Saturday except the forty-eighth Saturday; their break-fast, meaning their feast day, is the Sunday after that. The Jewish break-fast is that they eat for seven days from the fifteenth of the seventh month of their calendar, beginning before the Roman year by a month, corresponding to Moses and his people. As for the Jewish break-fast, as in al-Hidayah and others, it is not a famous day among them, unless it is said that it means the day they break their fast, for they fast by the text of the Torah for thirty-six days... end. The author's saying: 'al-Diyas'—al-Ramli said, al-Mutarrizi said: al-Diyasah in food is that it is trodden by the feet of beasts and repeated treading means until it becomes straw. Al-Diyas is polishing the sword, and the jurists' use of it in the place of al-Diyasah is either laxity or a mistake... end. His saying: 'Muhammad ibn al-Fadl said: it invalidates the sale.' We previously mentioned at the author's saying in the Book of Sales: 'and valid with an immediate price and a known term' from al-Khaniyya that the invalidity is the saying of Abu Hanifa and that it is correct. In Ghayat al-Bayan, Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi said: If it is said that slight ignorance is tolerated in one place does not indicate that deferment to these unknown times is tolerated; do you not see that the dower tolerates slight ignorance as it tolerates ignorance of description, yet stipulating these terms is not valid in it... end. Then he said: The answer to this section is not preserved in the books, and among our teachers there is difference of opinion on it; the most correct is that these terms are established in the dower because there is no doubt that stipulating these terms does not affect the original marriage contract, unlike sale, so this remains a defect in the debt established by the contract. His saying: 'And we previously mentioned that if he sells etc.' Al-Ramli said: He previously mentioned that he gives fatwa that it is deferred until a month; he said: as if because
Source pages p. 145

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq is a commentary on the matn of Kanz al-Daqaiq in the chapter of invalid sales. The core ruling is that a sale with a deferred payment tied to an uncertain future event—such as Nowruz, Mihrajan, the Christian fast, or the Jewish break-fast—is invalid (fasid) if the term is not known to both parties at the time of contract. The reason given is 'jahalah al-ajal' (ignorance of the term), which leads to dispute (munaza'ah) because sale transactions are based on mutual agreement and bargaining (mumakasah). If both parties know the term, the sale is valid. The author then clarifies the definitions of Nowruz and Mihrajan based on astronomical positions (sun entering Aries for Nowruz, Libra for Mihrajan), noting that these are seasonal markers. He also distinguishes between the Christian fast (which is unknown by days because it's a movable fast) and their break-fast (Easter, which is known by days), and similarly for Jews. The commentary expands to include other uncertain times like the arrival of pilgrims, harvest, threshing, and vintage—all invalid due to variability. A key nuance: if the deferment is made after the contract is valid (e.g., by subsequent agreement), it may be permissible according to some scholars, but the original stipulation in the contract causes invalidity. The passage also discusses surety (kafala) with such terms, which is valid because slight ignorance is tolerated in surety. Finally, there is an intra-madhhab dispute: Muhammad ibn al-Fadl says postponement after a valid contract invalidates the sale, while Muhammad al-Shaybani says it is valid as a voluntary deferment. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that the invalidity is the statement of Abu Hanifa and it is correct. The text emphasizes that the criterion is the knowledge of both parties; if only one knows, the sale is still invalid.

Key Terms
النيروز (al-Nayruz): Nowruz, the first day of spring/summer when the sun enters Aries; a Persian festival.
المهرجان (al-Mihrajan): Mihrajan, the first day of autumn/winter when the sun enters Libra; another Persian festival.
الجهالة (al-Jahalah): Ignorance or uncertainty regarding a contractual term, leading to invalidity in sales.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi view, what happens to a valid sale if the parties subsequently agree to defer payment to an uncertain future time?
A) The sale remains valid, and the deferment is a separate promise.
B) The sale becomes fasid (invalid).
C) The sale becomes void from the start.
D) The sale is valid only if the deferment is written.

Key Takeaway
For a sale with deferred payment, both parties must know the term at the time of contract; a later change to an uncertain term invalidates the sale according to the relied-upon Hanafi position.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

8 min
Sales with Uncertain Future Payment Terms
Explains the prohibition of selling with uncertain future payment terms.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sales with uncertain payment terms, explain why the term causes fasad, and distinguish between a term stipulated in the contract and one added later.

Core Idea
A sale is fasid if its payment term is tied to an uncertain event, because uncertainty leads to dispute.

In this passage from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqaiq, we examine a classic Hanafi ruling on sales where the payment deadline is linked to events like harvest or pilgrimage. The key insight is that uncertainty in timing (jahala) invalidates the term, but the ruling depends on whether the term was part of the original contract or added later. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and internal dispute.

Guided Path
1
Identify the events and their legal status
The passage lists four events: pilgrimage arrival, harvest, threshing, and grape-picking. Note that each is a natural or seasonal event without a fixed date.
The commentator explains the linguistic variations of these terms.
2
Understand the illa (cause) for invalidity
The reason (illa) for the ruling is that these events can occur early or late, leading to uncertainty (gharar) and potential dispute between buyer and seller.
This is a rational proof (ta'lil) based on avoidance of dispute.
3
Distinguish between original term and added term
The commentary emphasizes that the invalidity applies only when the uncertain term is stipulated in the original contract (fi sulb al-aqd). If the term is added later, it is considered postponement of a debt, which is permissible.
This distinction is crucial for fatwa practice.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute
Two narrations from Muhammad ibn al-Fadl and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani: one holds that even adding the term later invalidates the sale, the other holds it valid because the delay is a gift.
The relied-upon view is that the sale is fasid if the term is in the original contract; the later addition view is mufta bihi according to some.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and practical application
The operative position is that selling with an uncertain term is fasid. However, if the sale was valid and then the term is added, it is acceptable according to the stronger view.
When issuing a fatwa, the mufti must distinguish these two scenarios.

كتاب البيع باب البيع الفاسد

الحاج والحصاد والدياس والقطاف ولو كفل إلى هذه الأوقات جاز ولو أسقط الأجل قبل حلوله

قوله : ( وإلى قدوم الحاج والحصاد والدياس والقطاف أي لا يجوز البيع إلى هذه الآجال لأنها تتقدم وتتأخر والحصاد بكسر الحاء وفتحها ومثله القطاف وهو للعنب، والدياس وهو دوس الحب بالقدم ليتكسر وأصله الدواس بالواو لأنه من الدوس قلبت الواو ياء للكسرة قبلها، ولم يذكر الجذاذ وذكره في الهداية واختلف في معناه فقيل جز الصوف من ظهور الغنم، وقيل جذاذا النخل ؛ قاله الحلواني. وفي نسخ الهداية وفتح القدير بالزاي المكررة أخت الراء. وذكر الزيعلي أنه بالذال المعجمة عام في قطع الثمار وبالمهملة خاص في قطع النخل .اهـ. فعلى هذا لم يكن بالزاي وذكره في المصباح في فصل الذال المعجمة وفصل الزاي وأن كلاً منهما بمعنى قطع وهما من باب قتل. قيد بالبيع إلى هذه الآجال لأنه لو باع مطلقاً عنها ثم أجل الثمن إليها لم يفسد لكونه تأجيلاً للدين فالمفسد ما كان في صلب العقد؛ كذا في الهداية وفي فتاوى قاضيخان : تبايعا بيعاً جائزاً ثم أخر الثمن إلى الحصاد قال محمد بن الفضل : يفسد البيع. وعن محمد لا يفسد ويصح التأخير لأن التأخير بعد البيع تبرع فيقبل التأجيل إلى مجهول كالكفالة إليها، وقدمنا أنه لو باع بثمن مؤجل ولم يعينه ففيه خلاف، وفي القنية : باع بألف نصفه نقد ونصفه إلى رجوعه من دهشان فهو فاسد والفتوى على انصرافه إلى شهر. وبينا مسائل التأجيل عند قوله وصح بثمن حال ومؤجل» والله أعلم
Book of Sale, Chapter of Invalid Sale. The pilgrimage, harvest, threshing, grape-picking, and if he is surety to these times it is permissible, and if he drops the term before its due it is valid. His statement: 'And to the arrival of the pilgrimage, harvest, threshing, and grape-picking' meaning that selling to these terms is not permissible because they may come early or late. Harvest: with kasr of the ha and fath of it, and similarly grape-picking which is for grapes, and threshing which is treading grain with the foot to break it, its origin is 'dawas' with waw because it is from 'daws', the waw was changed to ya due to the kasra before it. He did not mention 'jidadh' and it is mentioned in al-Hidayah, and there is disagreement on its meaning: some say it is shearing wool from sheep, some say it is cutting of palm trees; al-Halwani said it. In some copies of al-Hidayah and Fath al-Qadir it is with the repeated za (like ra). al-Zayla'i mentioned that with the dotted dhal it is general for cutting fruits, and with the undotted dal it is specific for cutting palm trees. So according to this it is not with za, and he mentioned it in al-Misbah in the chapter of dotted dhal and the chapter of za, and that each means cutting, and they are from the category of qatala. He restricted to selling to these terms because if he sold absolutely and then postponed the price to them, it does not become invalid because it is postponement of a debt; the invalidating factor is what is in the substance of the contract; thus in al-Hidayah. And in Fatawa Qadikhan: They made a valid sale then delayed the price to harvest; Muhammad ibn al-Fadl said: the sale becomes invalid. And from Muhammad: it does not become invalid and the delay is valid because delay after sale is a gift, so it accepts postponement to an unknown like surety to it. And we have presented that if he sold with a deferred price and did not specify it, there is a difference of opinion. And in al-Qunya: He sold for a thousand, half cash and half to his return from Dahshan, so it is invalid, and the fatwa is that it is deferred to a month. And we presented the issues of postponement at his statement: 'and it is valid with a present price and a deferred price.' And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 146

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqaiq explains the ruling on sales where the payment term is tied to uncertain future events such as the arrival of the pilgrimage, harvest, threshing, or grape-picking. The author states that such sales are invalid (la yajuz) because these events can occur early or late, causing uncertainty (jahala) that leads to dispute. The commentator defines each term: 'hasad' (harvest) can be pronounced with kasr or fath of the ha; 'qitaf' is specifically for grapes; 'diyas' is threshing by treading. He also discusses the word 'jidadh' which is mentioned in al-Hidayah, noting different interpretations: some say it means shearing wool, others cutting palm trees. The correct reading is with dhal (dotted) or dal (undotted) depending on the meaning. The key point is that the invalidity is specific to cases where the uncertain term is stipulated in the original contract (fi sulb al-aqd). If the sale was initially unconditional and the term is added later, it is merely postponement of a debt and does not invalidate the sale. However, there is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Muhammad ibn al-Fadl holds that even adding the term later invalidates the sale, while another narration from Muhammad (al-Shaybani) holds it valid because the delay is a gift. The commentator also mentions that if the price is deferred but the term is left unspecified, there is a difference of opinion, and the fatwa in some cases is to default to a month. This passage is a ruling with proof, where the proof is the rational cause (illa) of uncertainty leading to dispute. The relied-upon position is that such sales are fasid (invalid but curable).

Key Terms
الأجل المجهول (al-ajal al-majhool): A future payment term that is uncertain because it is tied to an event whose timing is unknown.
البيع الفاسد (al-bay' al-fasid): A sale that is invalid due to a defect in a condition, curable by removing the defect.
الحصاد (al-hasad): The time of harvesting crops, used as a payment term in sales.
الحاج (al-haj): The pilgrimage season, used as a payment term in sales.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is selling with payment due at harvest time considered invalid in the Hanafi school?
A) Because harvest may not occur at all.
B) Because the timing is uncertain and leads to dispute.
C) Because the price is unknown.
D) Because both parties must know the exact date.

Key Takeaway
A sale is fasid if the payment term is tied to an uncertain event; the illa is the potential for dispute due to unknown timing.

Kafalah to Uncertain Terms and Curing Fasid Sale by Dropping the Term
Explains that kafalah allows slight uncertainty, and that dropping a defective term before due can cure the sale.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on kafalah to uncertain terms and explain when dropping the term cures a fasid sale, identifying the intra-Hanafi dispute with Zufar.

Core Idea
Kafalah tolerates slight uncertainty; dropping a defective term before its due can cure the sale if the defect is in a condition.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq expands on two related rulings: the validity of suretyship (kafalah) when the payment term is uncertain but slight, and the effect of waiving an uncertain payment term in a sale. The author argues that slight uncertainty is tolerated in kafalah but not in sale. However, if the buyer drops the uncertain term before it becomes due, the sale becomes valid because the defect was in an additional condition, not the essence. An intra-Hanafi dispute with Imam Zufar is highlighted.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Rulings
Find the two distinct rulings in the passage: (1) kafalah to uncertain times is valid, (2) dropping the term before due makes the sale valid. Note the scope of each.
The passage starts with 'And if he is surety to these times' and later 'And if he drops the term before its due'.
2
Analyze the Reasoning for Kafalah
Understand why kafalah tolerates slight uncertainty: because it can tolerate even greater uncertainty in the principal debt, and by qiyas it tolerates in the description. Contrast with sale, which requires certainty.
The qiyas: kafalah for 'what has melted on so-and-so' is valid, so a fortiori for a slightly uncertain term.
3
Understand the Rule for Dropping the Term
The buyer may drop the invalidating term before the stated event. The sale becomes valid because the defect was in a superfluous condition (shart za'id), not the essence. Compare with cases where the defect is in the essence (e.g., dirham sale).
Key distinction: condition vs. essence. If the defect is in the essence, dropping does not cure.
4
Compare Abu Hanifa and Zufar
For close uncertainty (e.g., harvest), Abu Hanifa: dropping before the event cures; Zufar: never cures. For far uncertainty (e.g., wind), Abu Hanifa: dropping before separation and payment cures; Zufar: never cures. Note the consensus when the time passes or they separate without dropping.
The passage cites al-Haqa'iq for this detail.
5
Apply the Distinction
Given a scenario, determine whether the defect is in a condition or in the essence, and whether the timing of dropping is proper. Then state the ruling according to the mufta bihi.
The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's position.

قوله : (ولو كفل إلى هذه الأوقات (جاز) لأن الجهالة اليسيرة متحملة في الكفالة وهذه الجهالة[؟] من له يسيرة مستدركة لاختلاف الصحابة فيها، ولأنه معلوم الأصل ألا ترى أنها تحتمل الجهالة في أصل الدين بأن تكفل بما ذاب على فلان ففي الوصف أولى بخلاف البيع فإنه لا يحتملها في أصل الثمن فكذا في وصفه. قيد بهذه الأوقات لأنه لو كفل إلى هبوب الريح فهي باطلة لأنها متفاحشة وتأتي في بابها قوله : (ولو أسقط الأجل قبل حلوله صح) أي لو أسقط الأجل وهو المشتري الأجل المفسد للبيع قبل الحصاد والدياس والقطاف وقدوم الحاج انقلب البيع صحيحاً لأن الفساد كان للمنازعة وقد ارتفع قبل تقرره وهذه الجهالة في شرط زائد لا في صلب العقد فيمكن إسقاطه بخلاف بيع الدرهم بالدرهمين لا ينقلب صحيحاً بإسقاط الدرهم الزائد لأن الفساد في صلب العقد، وبخلاف إسقاط الأجل في النكاح الموقت لكونه متعة وهو غير عقد النكاح. وقال في مختصر القدوري: تراضيا على إسقاطه بالتثنية وخالفه المؤلف فوحد الضمير لقوله في الهداية : وقوله في الكتاب تراضيا» خرج وفاقاً لأن من له الأجل يستبد بإسقاطه لأنه خالص حقه. وقيد بهذه الآجال لأنهما لو تبايعا إلى هبوب الريح أو مطر السماء ثم تراضيا على إسقاطه لا ينقلب العقد جائزاً لأن هذا ليس بأجل بل الأجل هو المعهود في الشرع في السلم واليمين ليقضين دينه آجلاً فقوله وفي القنية» إلى قوله «فهو فاسد» اعتراض بين قوله «وقدمنا أنه لو باع بثمن مؤجل ولم يعين ففيه خلاف وبين قوله «والفتوى على انصرافه إلى شهر أو أنه لمسألة القنية وتكون العلة في ذلك أن العادة للذهاب والإياب عندهم شهر فصار كأنه ضربه بعينه وهذا هو الظاهر تأمل. قول المصنف : ولو أسقط أجل قبل حلوله صح) قال الرملي : وقيده في شرح المجمع لابن ملك بالمجلس وعبارته : وقيدنا بقولنا قبل التفرق لأنه لو تفرقا قبل ذلك تأكد الفساد ولا ينقلب جائزاً بالاتفاق من الحقائق فليتأمل كذا رأيت بخط شيخ الإسلام ابن عبد الله محمد الغزي رحمه الله تعالى وفيه نظر، فإن هذا القيد لم يذكره غيره، وصريح كلام الشارح بخلافه فقد قال: أي لو باع إلى هذه الآجال ثم أسقط المشتري الأجل قبل أن يأخذ الناس في الحصاد والدياس وقبل قدوم الحاج جاز ومثله يصد ما في هذا الشرح وغيره ولو كان شرطاً لاقتصر عليه ولم يذكر مجيء الأجل إذا ذكره والحالة هذه لغو فتأمل . اهـ ملخصاً. أقول: وقد راجعت الحقائق شرح المنظومة النسفية فوجدت ما يفيد خلال ما نقله ابن الملك عنها ونص عبارتها في باب ما اختص به زفر اعلم أن البيع بأجل مجهول لا يجوز إجماعاً، سواء كانت الجهالة متقاربة كالحصاد والدياس مثلاً أو متفاوتة كهبوب الريح وقدوم واحد من سفره، فإن أبطل المشتري الأجل المجهول المتقارب قبل محله وقبل فسخ العقد بالفساد انقلب البيع جائزاً عندنا، وعند زفر لا ينقلب. ولو مضت المدة قبل إبطال الأجل تأكل الفساد ولا ينقلب جائزاً إجماعاً، وإن أبطل المشتري الأجل المجهول المتفاوت قبل التفرق ونقد الثمن انقلب جائزاً عندنا وعند زفر لا ينقلب جائزاً. ولو تفرقا قبل الإطال تأكد الفساد ولا ينقلب جائزاً إجماعاً من شرح الطحاوي في أول السلم. قلت: ذكر أبو حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى الأجل المجهول مطلقاً وقد بينت أن إسقاط كل واحد مؤقت بوقت على حدة
His statement: 'And if he is surety to these times (it is permissible) because slight uncertainty is tolerated in surety, and this uncertainty ... is slight, overlooked due to difference among the Companions, and because it is known in origin; do you not see that it tolerates uncertainty in the principal debt if he is surety for what has melted on so-and-so, so in the description it is more fitting, unlike sale which does not tolerate it in the principal price, so likewise in its description. It is restricted to these times because if he is surety to the blowing of the wind, it is invalid because it is grossly uncertain, and it will come in its chapter. His statement: 'And if he drops the term before its due (it is valid)' meaning if the buyer drops the term that invalidates the sale before harvest, threshing, grape-picking, and arrival of the pilgrimage, the sale becomes valid because the invalidity was due to dispute and it has been removed before its establishment, and this uncertainty is in an additional condition, not in the substance of the contract, so it can be dropped, unlike the sale of a dirham for two dirhams which does not become valid by dropping the extra dirham because the invalidity is in the substance of the contract, and unlike dropping the term in a temporary marriage because it is mut'ah and is not the marriage contract. And he said in Mukhtasar al-Quduri: 'They both agreed on dropping it' with dual, and the author disagreed and used singular pronoun because of his statement in al-Hidayah: 'And his statement in the book 'they both agreed' came out in agreement because the one who has the term can drop it alone since it is his pure right. And it is restricted to these terms because if they sold to the blowing of wind or rain from the sky and then agreed on dropping it, the contract does not become valid because this is not a term; rather the term is what is customary in shari'ah in salam and oath to pay his debt later. So his statement 'and in al-Qunya' to his statement 'so it is invalid' is an objection between his statement 'and we have presented that if he sold with a deferred price and did not specify it there is a difference' and his statement 'and the fatwa is that it is deferred to a month' or that it is for the issue of al-Qunya and the cause is that the custom for going and coming among them is a month, so it is as if he specified it, and this is apparent, ponder. The author's statement: 'and if he drops the term before its due it is valid' – al-Ramli said: Ibn Malik in his commentary on al-Majma' restricted it to the session, and his expression: 'We restricted it by our saying before separation because if they separated before that, the invalidity becomes confirmed and it does not become valid by agreement, from al-Haqa'iq, so let it be pondered.' I saw in the handwriting of Shaykh al-Islam Ibn Abd Allah Muhammad al-Ghazzi that there is consideration, for this restriction was not mentioned by others, and the explicit words of the commentator are contrary to it, for he said: 'If he sold to these terms then the buyer dropped the term before the people start harvest and threshing and before the arrival of the pilgrimage, it becomes valid', and similarly what is confirmed in this commentary and others, and if it were a condition he would have restricted it and not mentioned the arrival of the term, since if he mentioned it in this state it is superfluous, so ponder. Summary. I say: I have reviewed al-Haqa'iq Sharh al-Manzumat al-Nasafiyyah and found what benefits during what Ibn Malik transmitted from it, and the text of its expression in the chapter special to Zufar: 'Know that selling with an unknown term is not permissible by consensus, whether the uncertainty is close like harvest and threshing, or far like the blowing of wind and the arrival of someone from his travel. If the buyer annuls the close unknown term before its place and before dissolution of the contract due to invalidity, the sale becomes valid according to us, and according to Zufar it does not become valid. If the time passes before annulment of the term, the invalidity becomes established and it does not become valid by consensus. And if the buyer annuls the far unknown term before separation and payment of the price, it becomes valid according to us, and according to Zufar it does not become valid. And if they separate before annulment, the invalidity becomes confirmed and it does not become valid by consensus, from Sharh al-Tahawi at the beginning of al-Salam. I say: Abu Hanifa mentioned the unknown term absolutely, and I have shown that the dropping of each is limited to its own time separately.'
Source pages p. 146

Commentary
This passage continues the commentary on the same matn phrase, focusing on two additional rulings: (1) suretyship (kafalah) to these uncertain times is valid (jā'iz), and (2) dropping the term before its due date makes the sale valid (sahih). For kafalah, the reason given is that slight uncertainty (jahāla yasīra) is tolerated in surety contracts, unlike sale. The text argues that since kafalah can even tolerate uncertainty in the principal debt (e.g., being surety for 'what has melted on so-and-so'), it certainly tolerates uncertainty in the description of the term. This is contrasted with sale, which requires certainty in both the principal price and its description. The passage then addresses dropping the term: if the buyer drops the invalidating term before the stated event (harvest, etc.), the sale becomes valid. This is because the invalidity was due to potential dispute, which is removed before it materializes. The defect is in an additional condition (shart zā'id), not in the essence of the contract, so it can be dropped, unlike cases where the defect is in the essence (e.g., selling one dirham for two, or temporary marriage). The passage also discusses a restriction mentioned by some scholars that dropping must occur before the parties separate (tafarruq), but the commentator prefers the view that dropping any time before the event is sufficient, citing al-Haqa'iq. A significant intra-Hanafi dispute is presented: Imam Zufar holds that dropping does not cure the sale, while the majority (including Abu Hanifa) hold that it does, with differences based on the degree of uncertainty (close vs. far) and timing. The commentator concludes that the relied-upon position is that of Abu Hanifa. This lesson is an intra-Hanafi dispute with rational arguments.

Key Terms
الكفالة (al-kafalah): A contract of suretyship where one person guarantees the debt or obligation of another.
إسقاط الأجل (isqat al-ajal): The act of waiving or canceling the future payment term by the person entitled to it (the buyer).
الجهالة اليسيرة (al-jahalah al-yasirah): Slight uncertainty that is tolerated in certain contracts like kafalah but not in sale.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when does dropping a far-unknown term cure the sale according to Abu Hanifa?
A) Before the event and before separation.
B) Only before the event.
C) Only before separation.
D) Any time after the event.

Key Takeaway
Kafalah enters with slight uncertainty; a sale with uncertain term can be cured by dropping it before due, provided the defect is in a condition.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
6 min
Dropping an Unknown Deferment: Curing a Defective Sale
Intra-Hanafi dispute on curing a defective sale by dropping an unknown deferment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between close and extreme unknown deferments in a sale and apply the Hanafi ruling on dropping them before maturity or before separation.

Core Idea
Dropping an unknown deferment before maturity can validate a sale, but only if the defect is ancillary and the buyer exercises his right.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute regarding sales with unspecified future payment dates. The key issue is whether the buyer's voluntary cancellation of the ambiguous deferment can cure the initial invalidity. We will examine the positions of Abu Hanifa, the Sahibayn, and Zufar, and understand the conditions under which dropping is effective.

Guided Path
1
Identify the initial defect
Recognise that a sale with an unknown deferment (ajal majhool) is fasid because the potential for future dispute (gharar) invalidates the contract.
The defect is not in the essence of the contract but in an ancillary condition.
2
Distinguish close vs. extreme ajal
Close deferments (e.g., harvest, threshing) are seasonally known; extreme deferments (e.g., blowing wind) are highly uncertain. Different rules apply for dropping.
The Hanafi school treats close deferments more leniently.
3
Analyse the effect of dropping the ajal
If the buyer drops the deferment before it matures (for close ajal) or before the parties separate (tafarruq) for extreme ajal, the cause of dispute is removed and the sale becomes valid.
Only the buyer can drop it, as it is his right. Dropping after maturity or tafarruq is ineffective.
4
Contrast with Zufar's position
Zufar holds that dropping does not cure because the defect is inherent. The majority (Abu Hanifa & Sahibayn) differs.
Zufar's view is an acknowledged intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
5
Apply the mufta bihi ruling
The relied-upon position is that of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn: for close ajal, dropping before maturity cures; for extreme ajal, dropping before tafarruq cures.
This is the operative ruling for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب البيع باب البيع الفاسد من له يسيرة مستدركة لاختلاف الصحابة فيها، ولأنه معلوم الأصل ألا ترى أنها تحتمل الجهالة في أصل الدين بأن تكفل بما ذاب على فلان ففي الوصف أولى بخلاف البيع فإنه لا يحتملها في أصل الثمن فكذا في وصفه. قيد بهذه الأوقات لأنه لو كفل إلى هبوب الريح فهي باطلة لأنها متفاحشة وتأتي في بابها قوله : (ولو أسقط الأجل قبل حلوله صح) أي لو أسقط الأجل وهو المشتري الأجل المفسد للبيع قبل الحصاد والدياس والقطاف وقدوم الحاج انقلب البيع صحيحاً لأن الفساد كان للمنازعة وقد ارتفع قبل تقرره وهذه الجهالة في شرط زائد لا في صلب العقد فيمكن إسقاطه بخلاف بيع الدرهم بالدرهمين لا ينقلب صحيحاً بإسقاط الدرهم الزائد لأن الفساد في صلب العقد، وبخلاف إسقاط الأجل في النكاح الموقت لكونه متعة وهو غير عقد النكاح. وقال في مختصر القدوري: تراضيا على إسقاطه بالتثنية وخالفه المؤلف فوحد الضمير لقوله في الهداية : وقوله في الكتاب تراضيا» خرج وفاقاً لأن من له الأجل يستبد بإسقاطه لأنه خالص حقه. وقيد بهذه الآجال لأنهما لو تبايعا إلى هبوب الريح أو مطر السماء ثم تراضيا على إسقاطه لا ينقلب العقد جائزاً لأن هذا ليس بأجل بل الأجل هو المعهود في الشرع في السلم واليمين ليقضين دينه آجلاً فقوله وفي القنية» إلى قوله «فهو فاسد» اعتراض بين قوله «وقدمنا أنه لو باع بثمن مؤجل ولم يعين ففيه خلاف وبين قوله «والفتوى على انصرافه إلى شهر أو أنه لمسألة القنية وتكون العلة في ذلك أن العادة للذهاب والإياب عندهم شهر فصار كأنه ضربه بعينه وهذا هو الظاهر تأمل. قول المصنف : ولو أسقط أجل قبل حلوله صح) قال الرملي : وقيده في شرح المجمع لابن ملك بالمجلس وعبارته : وقيدنا بقولنا قبل التفرق لأنه لو تفرقا قبل ذلك تأكد الفساد ولا ينقلب جائزاً بالاتفاق من الحقائق فليتأمل كذا رأيت بخط شيخ الإسلام ابن عبد الله محمد الغزي رحمه الله تعالى وفيه نظر، فإن هذا القيد لم يذكره غيره، وصريح كلام الشارح بخلافه فقد قال: أي لو باع إلى هذه الآجال ثم أسقط المشتري الأجل قبل أن يأخذ الناس في الحصاد والدياس وقبل قدوم الحاج جاز ومثله يصد ما في عبارتها في باب ما اختص به زفر اعلم أن البيع بأجل مجهول لا يجوز إجماعاً، سواء كانت الجهالة متقاربة كالحصاد والدياس مثلاً أو متفاوتة كهبوب الريح وقدوم واحد من سفره، فإن أبطل المشتري الأجل المجهول المتقارب قبل محله وقبل فسخ العقد بالفساد انقلب البيع جائزاً عندنا، وعند زفر لا ينقلب. ولو مضت المدة قبل إبطال الأجل تأكل الفساد ولا ينقلب جائزاً إجماعاً، وإن أبطل المشتري الأجل المجهول المتفاوت قبل التفرق ونقد الثمن انقلب جائزاً عندنا وعند زفر لا ينقلب جائزاً. ولو تفرقا قبل الإطال تأكد الفساد ولا ينقلب جائزاً إجماعاً من شرح الطحاوي في أول السلم. قلت: ذكر أبو حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى الأجل المجهول مطلقاً وقد بينت أن إسقاط كل واحد مؤقت بوقت على حدة
Book of sales, chapter of invalid sale. [...] he said: (And if he drops the deferment before its maturity, it is valid) meaning if the buyer drops the deferment that made the sale invalid before harvest, threshing, grape-pressing, and the arrival of the pilgrim, the sale becomes valid because the invalidity was due to dispute and it was removed before its establishment. This ignorance is in an extra condition, not in the essence of the contract, so it can be dropped, unlike the sale of a dirham for two dirhams which does not become valid by dropping the extra dirham because the invalidity is in the essence of the contract. [...] I say: I consulted al-Haqa'iq Sharh al-Manẓuma al-Nasafiyya and found that Zufar said that the sale with an unknown deferment is not valid unanimously. If the buyer invalidates the unknown deferment that is close before its time and before revocation of the contract due to invalidity, the sale becomes valid according to us, but according to Zufar it does not. If the period passes before invalidating the deferment, the invalidity is established and it does not become valid unanimously.
Source pages p. 147

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the effect of dropping an unknown deferment (ajal majhool) in a sale. The author explains that if a sale is made with a deferred payment that is specified by a future event (like harvest or the arrival of a pilgrim), and the buyer drops that deferment before it matures, the sale becomes valid because the defect (gharar) was in an ancillary condition, not in the core of the contract. This is contrasted with a sale of one dirham for two dirhams, which is invalid due to riba in the essence, so dropping the extra does not cure it. The commentator notes that according to al-Quduri, both parties agree to drop the condition, but the author of al-Hidayah points out that only the buyer has the right to drop it because it is his exclusive right. If the deferment is extremely unknown (like the blowing of wind), dropping it does not help because that is not a recognized deferment in Islamic law. The passage then quotes al-Ramli and Ibn Malik regarding the condition that the dropping must occur before the parties separate (tafarruq). Zufar holds that dropping an unknown deferment does not validate the sale even if it is close, while Abu Hanifa and the two disciples hold that it does. For extremely unknown deferments, it only works if done before separation and payment. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, with the condition that for close deferments, dropping before maturity suffices, while for wildly unknown deferments, dropping must occur before the parties separate.

Key Terms
أجل مجهول (ajal majhool): A deferred payment time that is not specified with certainty, e.g., tied to a future event like harvest or the arrival of a pilgrim.
إسقاط الأجل (isqat al-ajal): The act of the buyer voluntarily cancelling the deferred payment condition after the contract but before its maturity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a sale is made with payment deferred until harvest (an unknown ajal), and the buyer drops the deferment before harvest, what happens to the sale?
A) The sale remains invalid because the defect was in the essence.
B) The sale becomes valid because the defect was in an ancillary condition and was removed.
C) The sale becomes valid only if both parties agree to drop it.
D) The sale becomes valid only if the seller also agrees to drop it.

Key Takeaway
The buyer's voluntary dropping of an unknown deferment before maturity can transform a fasid sale into a valid one, provided the ajal is close; for extreme ajal, dropping must occur before the parties separate.

Combining a Free Person with a Slave in a Sale: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on sale mixing free and slave

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa, the Sahibayn, and Zufar on the validity of a sale combining a free person and a slave, and explain the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) of their disagreement.

Core Idea
A sale combining a free person with a slave is void unless separate prices are specified, according to the Sahibayn.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents an intra-Hanafi dispute over a single sale that includes a free person—who cannot be sold as property—together with a slave or other lawful items. The central question is whether the entire sale is void or whether the valid part (the slave) can be salvaged if the prices are separated. Understanding this dispute will sharpen your ability to trace how different usul principles (e.g., corrupt conditions vs. limiting invalidity to the unlawful part) yield different fiqh rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prohibited element
Recognize that a free person (hurr) is not a commodity (mal) and cannot be the subject of a sale. Therefore, including him in a sale introduces an invalid element.
The same applies to a dead carcass (maytah) which is also not a valid commodity.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and his reasoning
Abu Hanifa rules that the entire sale is batil (void) because the contract is one transaction (safqah wahidah) and the condition of accepting the free person is a corrupt condition (shart fasid) that vitiates the whole.
He draws an analogy to combining a slaughtered sheep and a dead carcass: both are void.
3
Explain the Sahibayn's position and their condition for validity
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad rule that if the seller specifies a separate price for each item (thaman li kull wahid), the sale is valid for the slave (qinn) because the invalidity is confined to the free person and does not extend to the lawful part.
They analogize to a marriage contract that includes both a lawful and an unlawful woman: the unlawful part is void but the lawful part stands.
4
Explain Zufar's position
Zufar voids the entire sale in all cases, whether or not separate prices are mentioned, because mixing lawful and unlawful corrupts the entire contract.
His position is stricter than the Sahibayn's and aligns partly with Abu Hanifa.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and the mufta bihi
The practical consequence: if separate prices are specified, the Sahibayn allow the slave's sale to stand; otherwise, all agree it is void. The mufta bihi (operative ruling) is the Sahibayn's view for facilitating transactions.
This preference is based on the principle of easing dealings (taysir al-mu'amalat).

قوله: (ومن جمع بين حر وعبد أو بين شاة ذكية وميتة بطل البيع فيهما وإن جمع بين عبد ومدبر أو بين عبده وعبد غيره أو بين ملك ووقف صح في القن وعبده والملك) أما الأول فهو قول أبي حنيفة. وقالا : يصح إن سمى لكل واحد ثمناً، وأفسد البيع زفر في الكل فالأصل عنده أنه إذا جمع بين حل وحرام فإنه يفسد في الكل فصل أو لا، وقاس الثاني على الأول إذا محلية البيع منتفية بالإضافة إلى الكل ولهما أن الفساد بقدر المفسد فلا يتعدى إلى القن كمن جمع بين أجنبية وأخته في النكاح بخلاف ما إذا لم يسم ثمن كل واحد منهما للجهالة. ولأبي حنيفة وهو الفرق بين الفصلين أن الحر لا يدخل تحت العقد أصلاً لأنه ليس بمال والبيع صفقة واحدة فكان القبول في الحر شرطاً للبيع في العبد، وهذا شرط فاسد بخلاف النكاح لأنه لا يبطل بالشروط الفاسدة، أما البيع في هؤلاء فموقوف وقد دخلوا تحت العقد لقيام المالية ولذا ينعقد في عبد الغير بإجازته، وفي المكاتب برضاه في الأصح، وفي المدبر بقضاء القاضي، وكذا في أم الولد عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف إلا أن المالك باستحقاقه المبيع وهؤلاء باستحقاقهم أنفسهم ردوا البيع فكان هذا إشارة إلى البقاء كما إذا اشترى عبدين وهلك أحدهما قبل القبض وهذا لا يكون شرط القبول في غير المبيع ولا بيعاً بالحصة ابتداء ولهذا لا يشترط بيان ثمن كل واحد فيه ومتروك التسمية عمداً كالميتة، وأم الولد والمكاتب اهـ. بحروفه. وتقدم ذلك أيضاً في كلام المؤلف في شرح قول المتن «وبثمن حال ومؤجل» أول كتاب البيوع وعزاه إلى السراج فتنبه لهذا فقد جعل الشيخ محمد الغزي ما ذكره عن ابن الملك من مسائل متنه التنوير وتبعه شارحه الحصكفي عليه ووقع لابن الكمال مثل ما لابن ملك قول المصنف : (ومن جمع بين حر وعبد قال الرملي : أو جمع بين دنين من الخل فإذا أحدهما خمر، وهذا إذا قال بعتهما، أما إذا قال بعت أحدهما فقبل الآخر صح في القن تصحيحاً لتصرفه كما في الخلاصة. وقوله أو بين شاة ذكية وميتة المراد بالميتة التي ماتت حتف أنفها كما قيده به في الدرر والغرر والنهر وذكر الاحتراز في شرحه فراجعه .اهـ. قوله: (فأفتى مفتيها هو مولانا أبو السعود جامع أشتات
His saying: (And whoever combines a free person and a slave, or between a slaughtered sheep and a dead [carcass], the sale is void in both. If he combines between a slave and a mudabbir, or between his own slave and another's slave, or between owned property and waqf, it is valid for the qinn, his own slave, and the owned property.) As for the first, it is the saying of Abu Hanifa. And the two said: It is valid if he specifies a price for each. And Zufar invalidated the sale in all cases. [...]
Source pages p. 147

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a single sale that combines a free person (who cannot be sold) with a slave or other lawful items. Abu Hanifa rules that the entire sale is void because the free person is not a commodity, and since it is one transaction, the condition that the buyer accepts the free person is a corrupt condition that invalidates the whole sale. The two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say the sale is valid if each item is given a separate price, as the invalidity is confined to the free person and does not extend to the slave. Zufar voids the entire sale because mixing lawful and unlawful corrupts all. The commentator then explains that for other combinations like a slave and a mudabbir (a slave promised freedom after the master's death) or a slave with another's slave, the sale is valid for the lawful part because those are all commodities. The text also clarifies that if a slave is sold with a dead carcass, it is void by Abu Hanifa's view. The passage ends with a remark about a fatwa by Abu al-Su'ud. The relied-upon position in practice is the one that validates the sale for the slave when separate prices are mentioned, as per the Sahibayn, though Abu Hanifa's view is also authoritative.

Key Terms
حر (hurr): A free human being, who cannot be the subject of a sale as they are not property.
مدبر (mudabbir): A slave who has been promised freedom upon the master's death (tadbir).
قن (qinn): A full slave with no promise of freedom, fully owned as property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

According to Abu Hanifa, if someone sells a free person together with a slave in one contract without specifying separate prices, what is the ruling?
A) The sale is valid for the slave but void for the free person.
B) The sale is void for both the slave and the free person.
C) The sale is valid if the buyer agrees.
D) The sale is valid only for the free person.

Key Takeaway
The Sahibayn's view that the slave's sale remains valid if separate prices are specified is the relied-upon position for facilitating transactions.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
12 min
Combining a Free Person and a Slave in One Sale
Sharh on Kanz al-Daqa'iq: expansion of ruling on mixed sales

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a sale combining a free person with a slave, distinguish the cases that void the entire contract, and explain the internal Hanafi ikhtilaf.

Core Idea
A sale including a non-property item (free person, carcass) is entirely void; including a property with defect preserves the valid part.

This lesson examines a key ruling in Hanafi sales law: what happens when a valid item (like a slave) is sold together with an invalid one (like a free person)? The answer depends on whether the invalid item can be property at all. We will explore the positions of Abu Hanifa, the two companions, and Zufar, and understand the legal reasoning behind each view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories in the matn
First, note that the matn distinguishes between combining a free person with a slave (or a slaughtered sheep with a carcass) – where the sale is void in both – and combining a slave with a mudabbar, another's slave, or owned property with waqf – where the sale is valid for the owned item.
The key difference lies in whether the invalid item can be property at all.
2
Analyze the first category: free person + slave
Abu Hanifa holds the sale void entirely because the free person is not property and cannot enter the contract. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say it is valid if each price is specified, as invalidity does not spread. Zufar voids it entirely.
The opposing argument: the corrupt condition only affects the invalid part.
3
Examine the reasoning (dalil) of each position
Sahibayn analogize to marriage where mixing permissible and impermissible women does not void the permissible. Abu Hanifa distinguishes because sales are more vulnerable to corrupt conditions. Zufar analogizes to mixing halal and haram in food.
The debate is over whether the invalid element spreads or remains confined.
4
Apply the ruling to the second category
When the invalid item is property (mudabbar, another's slave, waqf), the sale is valid for the owned item because the contract can include them conditionally. The invalid part does not void the valid part.
This shows that property status is the dividing line.
5
Synthesize the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
If a buyer and seller combine a free person and a slave without separate prices, the sale is void according to Abu Hanifa, so the slave is not transferred. According to the two companions, if prices are stated, the slave is transferred.
The fatwa today relies on Abu Hanifa's view for the first case.

Source Text

قوله: (ومن جمع بين حر وعبد أو بين شاة ذكية وميتة بطل البيع فيهما وإن جمع بين عبد ومدبر أو بين عبده وعبد غيره أو بين ملك ووقف صح في القن وعبده والملك) أما الأول فهو قول أبي حنيفة. وقالا : يصح إن سمى لكل واحد ثمناً، وأفسد البيع زفر في الكل فالأصل عنده أنه إذا جمع بين حل وحرام فإنه يفسد في الكل فصل أو لا، وقاس الثاني على الأول إذا محلية البيع منتفية بالإضافة إلى الكل ولهما أن الفساد بقدر المفسد فلا يتعدى إلى القن كمن جمع بين أجنبية وأخته في النكاح بخلاف ما إذا لم يسم ثمن كل واحد منهما للجهالة. ولأبي حنيفة وهو الفرق بين الفصلين أن الحر لا يدخل تحت العقد أصلاً لأنه ليس بمال والبيع صفقة واحدة فكان القبول في الحر شرطاً للبيع في العبد، وهذا شرط فاسد بخلاف النكاح لأنه لا يبطل بالشروط الفاسدة، أما البيع في هؤلاء فموقوف وقد دخلوا تحت العقد لقيام المالية ولذا ينعقد في عبد الغير بإجازته، وفي المكاتب برضاه في الأصح، وفي المدبر بقضاء القاضي، وكذا في أم الولد عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف إلا أن المالك باستحقاقه المبيع وهؤلاء باستحقاقهم أنفسهم ردوا البيع فكان هذا إشارة إلى البقاء كما إذا اشترى عبدين وهلك أحدهما قبل القبض وهذا لا يكون شرط القبول في غير المبيع ولا بيعاً بالحصة ابتداء ولهذا لا يشترط بيان ثمن كل واحد فيه ومتروك التسمية عمداً كالميتة، وأم الولد والمكاتب
اهـ. بحروفه. وتقدم ذلك أيضاً في كلام المؤلف في شرح قول المتن «وبثمن حال ومؤجل» أول كتاب البيوع وعزاه إلى السراج فتنبه لهذا فقد جعل الشيخ محمد الغزي ما ذكره عن ابن الملك من مسائل متنه التنوير وتبعه شارحه الحصكفي عليه ووقع لابن الكمال مثل ما لابن ملك قول المصنف : (ومن جمع بين حر وعبد قال الرملي : أو جمع بين دنين من الخل فإذا أحدهما خمر، وهذا إذا قال بعتهما، أما إذا قال بعت أحدهما فقبل الآخر صح في القن تصحيحاً لتصرفه كما في الخلاصة. وقوله أو بين شاة ذكية وميتة المراد بالميتة التي ماتت حتف أنفها كما قيده به في الدرر والغرر والنهر وذكر الاحتراز في شرحه فراجعه .اهـ.
It is correct: Whoever combines a free person and a slave, or a ritually slaughtered sheep and a carcass, the sale is void in both. But if he combines a slave and a mudabbar, or his own slave and another's slave, or owned property and waqf, it is valid in the owned slave, his slave, and the owned property.
Source pages p. 148

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq, expanding the ruling on combining valid and invalid items in a single sale. The author begins by restating the matn: If a free person (who is not property) and a slave are sold together, or a ritually slaughtered sheep and a carcass, the sale is void for both. This is the position of Abu Hanifa. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that the sale is valid if each item's price is specified, because the invalidity does not affect the valid item. Zufar goes further, declaring the entire sale void in all cases, analogizing to the mixing of permissible and prohibited. Abu Hanifa distinguishes: a free person cannot be subject to sale at all (not property), so including him creates a corrupt condition (shart fasid) for the slave's sale, voiding the whole. The second category (slave+mudabbar, etc.) involves items that are property, so the sale is valid for the owned item, while the other is not property or its sale is suspended. The commentary then cites various sources (Siraj al-Wahhaj, Fath al-Qadir, etc.) on related issues, such as selling with an invalid condition like a future event, or combining a valid price with wine. It clarifies that the key difference is whether the invalid element can enter the contract at all (free person cannot) or only has a defect (mudabbar, another's slave, waqf). The passage also notes that if one says 'I sold one of them' and the other accepts, the sale is valid for the valid item. The term 'carcass' is specified as an animal that died naturally, not slaughtered.

Key Terms
حر (hurr): A free person who is not subject to ownership or sale.
عبد (abd): A slave who is property and can be sold.
ميتة (maytah): An animal that died naturally, not slaughtered according to Islamic law; it is not permissible to sell or consume.
مدبر (mudabbar): A slave who has been promised freedom upon the master's death; considered property but his sale is subject to conditions.
وقف (waqf): An endowment of property for charitable purposes; it is owned by Allah and cannot be sold ordinarily, but may be sold under certain conditions.
قن (qinn): An owned slave (in full ownership), as opposed to a mudabbar or mukatab.
ملك (milk): Owned property (private ownership).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, why is a sale combining a free person and a slave entirely void, while a sale combining a slave and a mudabbar is valid for the slave?
A) Because a free person is not property, so including him introduces a corrupt condition that voids the whole contract.
B) Because the free person is like a carcass, which is impure.
C) Because the two companions objected to the sale.
D) Because the mudabbar is also a free person.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi sales law, including a non-property item like a free person voids the entire contract, whereas including a property item with a defect only suspends that part, preserving the valid part.

The Validity of a Sale Combining Waqf and Owned Property
Inter-madhhab dispute and critical refinement of a fatwa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that combining waqf and owned property in one sale does not invalidate the sale of the owned property, and to evaluate the counter-argument of the mufti of Constantinople.

Core Idea
Waqf is property, not a free person; its inclusion does not void the sale of the owned portion.

This lesson examines a significant fatwa dispute that arose in Constantinople: a sale that combined waqf endowment property with privately owned property in a single contract. The mufti of the city, Abū al-Suʿūd, ruled that the entire sale was invalid because the waqf is inalienable and its invalidity spreads to the owned property. However, the established Hanafi position, supported by authoritative texts, is that the sale of the owned property remains valid. We will trace the reasoning behind both views and identify the practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
According to the relied-upon (muftā bihi) Hanafi view, selling waqf property alone is bāṭil (void). However, when waqf and owned property are sold together in one transaction, the sale of the owned property is ṣaḥīḥ (valid) – the invalidity of the waqf part does not spread.
The waqf is considered property (māl), not a free person (ḥurr), so its restricted saleability does not affect other items in the same contract.
2
Identify the opponent and their argument
Abū al-Suʿūd, the mufti of Constantinople, argued that once a qāḍī rules on the validity and bindingness (luzūm) of a waqf, it becomes like a free person – absolutely inalienable. Therefore, its inclusion in a sale renders the entire contract void, including the owned portion.
The opponent's reasoning relies on a strong analogy between waqf and a free person, who cannot be sold.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response refutes the analogy: waqf is not like a free person because it can be sold under specific conditions – for istibdāl (replacement), if its yield declines, if it is usurped, or by a Ḥanbalī qāḍī's ruling. Moreover, Qāḍī Khān and the Ẓāhiriyya state that even after a qāḍī's ruling, claims of ownership in waqf can still be heard.
The existence of these exceptions proves that waqf is not absolutely inalienable like a free person.
4
Follow the textual arguments
The commentator cites authorities: Qāḍī Khān's fatwā, the Ẓāhiriyya, and the treatise Ḥusām al-Ḥukkām. They collectively show that combining waqf with owned property does not spoil the sale of the owned property. The mosque is an exception – like a free person – but ordinary waqf is not.
The distinction between a mosque (masjid) and other waqf is crucial: a mosque cannot be sold at all, so its invalidity spreads.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarāt al-khilāf)
The practical difference: According to the mufti's ruling, the entire sale would be void, forcing the parties to unwind the transaction. According to the correct Hanafi position, the sale of the owned property is valid and enforceable, protecting the buyer's ownership of that portion.
This dispute affects real estate transactions where waqf and private property are intermingled.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (فأفتى مفتيها هو مولانا أبو السعود جامع أشتات
كالمدبر، وفيما إذا جمع بين ملك ووقف روايتان وما ذكره المؤلف هو الصحيح لأن الوقف مال ولهذا ينتفع به انتفاع الأموال غير أنه لا يباع لأجل حق تعلق به وذلك لا يوجب فساد العقد فيما ضم إليه كالمدبر لكن أراد بالوقف ما ليس بمسجد فإن المسجد لو ضم إلى الملك فإنه يبطل فيهما لأن المسجد كالحر ؛ كذا ذكره الشارح . وقيده في التجنيس بالعامر لأن المسجد الخراب لو ضم إلى الملك لم يبطل في الملك لجواز بيع المسجد إذا خرب في أحد القولين فصار مجتهداً فيه كالمدبر، ولا يشكل ما في المحيط من أنه لو باع قرية ولم يستثن ما فيها من المساجد والمقابر فالأصح الصحة في الملك لأن ما فيها من المساجد والمقابر مستثنى عادة. ثم اعلم أنه قد وقعت حادثة في القسطنطونية هي جمع بين وقف وملك وباعهما صفقة واحدة فأفتى مفتيها بعدم الصحة في الملك كالوقف فاعترض عليه بأنه مخالف للأصح، فأجاب بأنه محمول على وقف لم يحكم بصحته ولزومه ليكون كالمدبر مجتهداً فيه أما ما قضى القاضي به فهو كالحر للزومه إجماعاً فيسري الفساد إلى الملك، لكن يرد عليه ما صرح به قاضيخان في فتاواه أن الوقف بعد القضاء تسمع دعوى الملك فيه وليس هو كالحر بدليل أنه لو ضم إلى ملك لا يفسد البيع في الملك، وهكذا في الظهيرية. وهذا لا يمكن تأويله فوجب الرجوع إلى الحق وهو إطلاق الوقف لأنه بعد القضاء وإن صار لازماً بالإجماع لكنه يقبل البيع بعد لزوم الوقف، إما بشرط الاستبدال وهو صحيح على قول أبي يوسف المفتى به أو بضعف غلته كما هو قولهما أو بورود غصب عليه ولا يمكن انتزاعه فللناظر بيعه كما في فتاوى قاضيخان أو بقضاء قاض حنبلي ببيعه فإن عنده بيع الوقف يجوز ويشتري ببدله ما هو خير منه كما في معراج الدراية فكيف يجعل الوقف كالحر مع وجود هذه الأسباب المجوزة لبيعه والله الموفق للصواب وإليه المرجع والمآب.
العلوم تغمده الله تعالى برضوانه؛ كذا في النهر . قال : ووافقه بعض علماء العصر من المصريين ومنهم شيخنا الأخ إلا أنه قال في شرحه هنا يرد عليه الخ. قوله : (ولكن يرد عليه ما صرح به قاضيخان الخ فإن قلت : يمكن حمل القضاء في كلام قاضيخان على القضاء بصحته لا بلزومه فلا يرد ما أفتى به مفتي الروم. قلت هو مطلق فيحمل على الكامل وهو القضاء بلزومه والله تعالى أعلم، ولأن في حمله على القضاء بلزومه فائدة بخلاف حمله على القضاء بالصحة فإنه لا فائدة فيه لأنه صحيح بدونه. أقول : وكلام شيخنا رحمه الله تعالى في شرحه هذا يفيد أن بيع الوقف فاسد وليس بباطل كما في الحر لكن في جواهر الفتاوى صرح ببطلانه وكلامه ظاهر في أنه لا يفيد الملك فليراجع والله تعالى أعلم ؛ كذا في حاشية الرملي. وفي الشرنبلالية صرح رحمه الله تعالى ببطلان بيع الوقف وأحسن بذلك إذ جعله في قسم البيع باطل إذ خلاف في بطلان بيع الوقف لأنه لا يقبل التمليك والتملك وغلط من جعله فاسداً وأفتى به من علماء القرن العاشر ورد كلامه في عصره بجمل رسائل ولنا فيه رسالة) هي حسام الحكام متضمنة لبيان فساد قوله وبطلان فتواه اهـ. ومراده بالغالط قاضي القضاة نور الدين الطرابلسي والعلامة الشيخ أحمد الشلبي كما ذكره في تلك الرسالة .
He said: 'The mufti of it is our master Abu al-Su'ud, compiler of scattered issues...' Like a mudabbar, and when combining owned property and waqf there are two narrations; what the author mentioned is correct because waqf is wealth... Then know that an incident occurred in Constantinople combining waqf and owned property...
Source pages p. 148

Commentary
This passage is a detailed discussion (critical refinement) of a fatwa issued by the mufti of Constantinople, Abu al-Su'ud, regarding a sale that combined waqf (endowment) property and privately owned property in a single transaction. The mufti ruled that the sale is invalid for both, similar to waqf alone. The commentator objects, stating that the relied-upon position (al-ashah) is that the sale is valid for the owned property because waqf, while not freely salable, is still property and its inclusion does not spread invalidity. The author then presents various arguments: Waqf after being established (by qadi's ruling) is not like a free person because it can still be sold under certain conditions (e.g., for istibdal, if its yield declines, or if usurped). The commentator cites Qadi Khan and other authorities to show that even after a qadi's ruling, waqf is not equivalent to a free person; a claim of ownership can still be heard, and combining it with owned property does not invalidate the sale of the owned property. The discussion also notes the difference between a mosque (which cannot be sold at all) and other waqf. The passage ends with a reference to a treatise (Husam al-Hukkam) refuting the mufti's view and labeling those who deem waqf sale merely fasid (corrupt) rather than batil (void) as mistaken. The commentator clarifies that the correct view is that selling waqf is batil because it cannot be owned or transferred, but some later scholars treated it as fasid. The practical outcome: the fatwa of Abu al-Su'ud was contested, and the authoritative position is that the sale of owned property combined with waqf is valid, while the waqf sale itself is batil.

Key Terms
وقف (waqf): Endowment property; its sale is generally invalid (bāṭil) but may be permissible under specific conditions like istibdāl.
ملك (milk): Privately owned property that can be sold freely.
مدبر (mudabbar): Slave promised freedom after master's death; his sale is valid but subject to conditions.
حر (ḥurr): Free person; not property and cannot be sold.
استبدال (istibdāl): Replacement of waqf property with another; sale of waqf for this purpose is valid according to Abū Yūsuf.
باطل (bāṭil): Void ab initio; does not transfer ownership.
فاسد (fāsid): Corrupt; a contract that is defective but may become valid if the defect is removed (though not in this case).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, if someone sells a waqf property together with his own property in a single sale, what is the ruling?
A) Both sales are void because waqf cannot be sold.
B) The sale of the owned property is valid, but the waqf property's sale is void.
C) The sale is valid for both if the prices are specified.
D) The sale is suspended until the qāḍī approves.

Key Takeaway
In a combined sale of waqf and owned property, the sale of the owned property is valid while the waqf sale is void (bāṭil); waqf is not equivalent to a free person and can be sold under specific conditions.
