Prohibited Sales: Townsman-Nomad and Friday Adhan
Commentary on prohibitions of town-nomad sale and Friday adhan sale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the townsman-nomad sale and the Friday adhan sale, explain the Quranic proof, and apply the principle that a prohibition for an external reason does not invalidate the contract.

Core Idea
A sale is valid but sinful if the prohibition targets an external factor, not the contract itself.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies two prohibited sales from Kanz al-Daqaiq. The first protects the nomad from exploitation by a townsman acting as broker. The second safeguards the Friday prayer from worldly distraction. The central legal insight is that the prohibition (karehana) is for an external reason, so the contract remains valid, though the act is sinful. Understanding this external-prohibition principle is key to distinguishing between invalidating defects and prohibitive restrictions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two prohibited sales
The text discusses 'al-hadir li al-badi' (townsman for nomad) and 'al-bay' 'inda adhan al-jumu'ah' (sale during Friday adhan). Understand the scenario: a townsman acting as broker for a nomad, and any sale after the second adhan for Jumu'ah.
Both involve a prohibition that does not affect the essence of the contract.
2
Locate the proof for the Friday adhan sale
The Quranic verse 'Wa dharu al-bay' (and leave sale) [Jumu'ah:9] is cited. Note the imperative form indicates a prohibition. The context is the Friday congregational prayer.
The proof is qati' in thubut and dalalah according to the author.
3
Understand the external-prohibition principle
The commentary explains that the prohibition is for a reason outside the contract's essence (ghayr dhat al-aqd) or its conditions of validity. Therefore, the sale is valid but the act is sinful (makruh tahrimi). This is a cornerstone of Hanafi fiqh in mu'amalat.
Distinguish this from prohibitions that affect the contract itself (e.g., selling alcohol).
4
Note the intra-Hanafi difference
Al-Nihayah holds that the Friday adhan sale is not even disliked when walking to the mosque. The commentator rejects this as contradicting the generality of the verse. The mufta bihi is the view of al-Hidayah: it is makruh.
This shows how later authorities weigh conflicting opinions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب البيع/ باب البيع الفاسد الحاضر للبادي والبيع عند أذان الجمعة. تفسير لضدها وهي الجائزة فالمعنى أنه نهى عن بيع السمسار وتعرضه فكأنه لما سئل عن نكتة نهي بيع الحاضر للبادي قال المقصود أن لا يكون له سمسار فنهى عنه بالسمسار؛ كذا في فتح القدير قوله : ( والبيع عند أذان الجمعة) لقوله تعالى وذروا البيع [الجمعة: ٩] ثم فيه إخلال بواجب السعي على بعض الوجوه وقد ذكرنا الأذان المعتبر فيه في كتاب الصلاة، وفي الهداية : كل ذلك يكره ولا يفسد به البيع لأن النهي لمعنى خارج زائد لا في صلب العقد ولا في شرائط الصحة . أطلقه فشمل ما إذا تبايعا وهما يمشيان إليها وما في النهاية من عدم الكراهة مشكل لإطلاق الآية فمن جوزه في بعض الوجوه يكون تخصيصاً وهو نسخ وهو يجوز بالرأي؛ كذا ذكره الشارح
Book of Sales / Chapter on Invalid Sales: The townsman for the nomad, and the sale at the Friday adhan. Explanation of its opposite, which is permissible. The meaning is that he prohibited the sale of the broker and his intermediation. It is as if when he was asked about the point of prohibiting the sale of the townsman for the nomad, he said: The intent is that he should not have a broker, so he prohibited it through the broker; as stated in Fath al-Qadir. His statement: (And the sale at the Friday adhan) because of the Almighty's saying: 'And leave sale' [Surah al-Jumu'ah:9]. Then it involves an omission of the duty of hastening to prayer in some respects, and we have mentioned the considered adhan in the Book of Prayer. In al-Hidayah: All of that is disliked and the sale is not invalidated because the prohibition is for an external additional reason, not in the essence of the contract nor in its conditions of validity. He applied it generally, so it includes when they transact while walking to it. What is in al-Nihayah of no dislike is problematic due to the generality of the verse. So whoever permits it in some respects would be making a specification, which is abrogation, and it is permissible by opinion; as stated by the commentator.
Source pages p. 165

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on two prohibitions from the matn of Kanz al-Daqaiq. The first prohibition is 'the townsman for the nomad' (al-hadir li al-badi). The commentator explains that the prohibition is against a townsman acting as a broker for a nomad, because the nomad is unaware of market prices and the townsman could exploit him. The reason is to protect the nomad from being overcharged. The second prohibition is a sale conducted during the Friday adhan. The proof is the Quranic command 'and leave sale' (Surah al-Jumu'ah:9). This act involves neglecting the duty of hastening to the Friday prayer. However, the commentator notes that according to al-Hidayah, both are makruh (disliked) but the contract is valid because the prohibition relates to an external factor, not the essence of the contract. The ruling applies generally, including when the parties are walking to the mosque. There is a conflicting view from al-Nihayah that it is not even makruh, but the commentator finds this problematic due to the general command of the Quran. The relied-upon position is that it is makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked).

Key Terms
الحاضر للبادي (al-hadir li al-badi): A townsman selling goods for a nomad (bedouin) who comes to the city.
بيع السمسار (bay' al-simsar): Sale through a broker or middleman.
البيع عند أذان الجمعة (al-bay' 'inda adhan al-jumu'ah): Any sale transaction conducted after the second adhan for the Friday congregational prayer has started.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling regarding a sale conducted during the Friday adhan according to al-Hidayah?
A) It is invalid (batil).
B) It is valid but makruh tahrimi.
C) It is permissible and not disliked.
D) It is haram and invalid.

Key Takeaway
A sale is valid if the prohibition targets an external factor; only defects in the contract's essence or conditions render it invalid.

The Permissibility of Auction-Style Sales (Bay' al-Min Yazid)
Commentary on the permissibility of auction-style sales

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on bidding sales and identify the evidential basis for its permissibility.

Core Idea
Auction sales are permissible because the Prophet himself conducted them and they fulfill a pressing need.

In this lesson, we examine the ruling on bay' al-min yazid (sale to the highest bidder). The Hanafi school holds that such sales are not only permissible but also commendable when needed. The commentator in Al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies that the prohibition implied by earlier scholars is not absolute, and he provides textual and rational evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject and initial ruling
Recognize that the passage addresses 'bay' al-min yazid' (bidding sale). The commentator begins by negating any dislike: 'لا بيع من يزيد' (no sale of one who increases), meaning it is not makruh.
The phrase 'لا بيع' here is idiomatic for 'no prohibition'.
2
Examine the textual proof (dalil naqli)
The commentary cites a hadith: the Prophet ﷺ sold a cup and a mat by bidding. This is a direct action (fi'l) of the Prophet, which in Hanafi usul indicates permissibility (ibaha) unless evidence suggests otherwise.
The hadith is considered authentic (sahih) and is taken from Sahih Muslim.
3
Analyze the rational proof (dalil aqli)
The commentator adds that this sale benefits the poor and serves a pressing need. In Hanafi law, need (hajah) can elevate a transaction from permissible to recommended.
The principle 'al-hajah tanzilu manzilat al-darurah' (need takes the place of necessity) applies here.
4
Confirm the Hanafi position
Based on the proof, the Hanafi ruling is that bidding sales are mubah (permissible) and not makruh. This is the relied-upon position (mufta bihi).
Any contrary opinion within the school is not mentioned; the position is established.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (لا بيع من يزيد) أي لا يكره لما قدمناه من عدم الإضرار وقد صح أن النبي ﷺ باع قدحاً وحلساً بيع من يزيد، ولأنه بيع الفقراء والحاجة ماسة إليه .
His statement: (No sale of one who increases) meaning it is not disliked because of what we have previously stated of no harm, and it is authentic that the Prophet ﷺ sold a cup and a mat by bidding, and because it is the sale of the poor and there is a pressing need for it.
Source pages p. 165

Commentary
This passage explains the ruling on what is known as 'bay' al-min yazid' (sale to the highest bidder), which is effectively an auction. The commentator clarifies that such a sale is not disliked (makruh). The reasoning is that it does not cause harm to anyone, and it is established by the Prophet's own action when he sold a drinking cup and a leather mat by bidding. Additionally, this type of sale particularly benefits the poor who may need to sell their items quickly, and there is a general need for such transactions. Therefore, it is considered permissible and even commendable.

Key Terms
بيع من يزيد (bay' al-min yazid): A sale where the item is offered to the highest bidder; essentially an auction.
قدح (qadah): A drinking cup or vessel.
حلس (hils): A mat or saddlecloth made of hair or wool.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is a bidding sale (bay' al-min yazid) considered permissible according to the passage?
A) It is not mentioned in any hadith.
B) The Prophet ﷺ himself practiced it.
C) It is similar to gambling.
D) It is only for the poor.

Key Takeaway
Bidding sales are permissible and not disliked in Hanafi fiqh because the Prophet's action and the need for such transactions override concerns of gharar.

Prohibition of Separating a Child from a Mahram Relative
Commentary on the ruling against separating a minor from a close relative in sale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on separating a child from a mahram relative, identify its proof from hadith, and apply the exceptions to given scenarios.

Core Idea
It is haram to separate a child from a mahram relative by sale, based on a hadith threat; exceptions exist for valid rights.

This lesson examines the classical Hanafi position on separating a child from a mahram relative through sale. The primary proof is a powerful hadith that threatens separation from loved ones in the afterlife. However, the school also recognises numerous exceptions based on valid rights and juristic preference (istihsan), making this a nuanced area of fiqh al-mu'amalat.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its subject
Locate the matn statement: 'ولا يفرق بين صغير وذي رحم محرم منه'. This prohibits separating a child from a mahram relative. Note that it applies to both young and old, and the relative must be mahram by blood.
The prohibition is general, covering all mahram relatives, not just mother and child.
2
Analyse the primary proof
The hadith 'من فرق بين والدة وولدها فرق الله بينه وبين أحبه يوم القيامة' establishes the prohibition. Also, the Prophet’s instruction to Ali to retrieve a sold brother shows the practical implication.
The hadith is ahad, so it gives zanni thubut, but the threat makes the ruling qati' al-dalala.
3
Understand the conditions
The prohibition applies only when both child and relative are owned by the same person. Also, the relative must be a mahram by blood (nasab) – not by marriage or breastfeeding (except when breastfeeding creates a milk-relationship equivalent to blood).
If they have different owners, selling one is not an issue.
4
Explore the exceptions for valid rights
The text lists permissible separations: when one is sold to pay a debt, for a crime compensation, due to a defect, when the owner is a non-Muslim forced to sell, or through emancipation, tadbir, istilad, kitabah, or sale to one who swore to free. Also, a child's sale with mother's consent if the child is adolescent.
The principle is to remove harm from others; the owner is not prevented from all dispositions.
5
Apply istihsan in cases of multiple relatives
If there are multiple mahram relatives of the same type (e.g., two maternal uncles), istihsan allows selling all but one. The commentary discusses degrees and types to determine the ruling.
Abu Yusuf differs in some cases; the mufta bihi is the majority view allowing sale of one.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (ولا يفرق بين صغير وذي رحم محرم منه) لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام من فرق بين والدة وولدها فرق الله بينه وبين أحبه يوم القيامة ووهب النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم لعلي غلامين صغيرين أخوين ثم قال له : ما فعل الغلامان؟ فقال: بعت أحدهما قال أدرك أدرك . ويروى أردد أردد ولأن الصغير يستأنس بالصغير وبالكبير والكبير يتعاهده فكان في بيع أحدهما قطع الاستئناس والمنع من التعاهد فيه ترك المرحمة على الصغار وقد أوعد النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم. ثم المنع معلول بالقرابة المحرمة للنكاح حتى لا يدخل فيه محرم غير قريب ولا قريب غير من محرم ولذا قيد بذي الرحم المحرم أي المحرم من جهة الرحم وإلا برد عليه ابن العم إذا كان أخاً من الرضاع فإنه رحم محرم وليس له هذا الحكم. وأطلقه فشمل الصغير والكبير ولا بد من اجتماعهما في ملكه حتى لو كان أحدهما له والآخر لغيره فلا بأس أحدهما. ولو قال ببيع المصنف إلا إذا كان التفريق بحق مستحق لكان أولى لأنه حينئذ يجوز التفريق كدفع بالجناية وبيعه بالدين ورده بالعيب لأن المنظور إليه دفع الضرر عن غيره لا الإضرار به؛ كذا في الهداية. ومن التفريق بحق ما في المبسوط ذمي له عبد له امرأة أمة ولدت منه فأسلم العبد وولده صغير فإنه يجبر الذمي على بيع العبد وابنه وإن كان تفريقاً بينه وبين أمه اهـ. ولا يرد على المصنف التفريق بإعتاق أحدهما بمال أو بغيره أو تدبيره أو استيلاد الأمة أو كتابة أحدهما فإنه جائز لأن مراده منع التفريق بالبيع أو الهبة أو الوصية أو غير ذلك من أسباب الملك كما في الجوهرة إذا لو منع عن الكل لصار المالك محجوراً عليه بمنعه من التصرف في ماله رأساً، وكذا لا يرد عليه ما لو كان في ملكه ثلاثة أحدهم صغير فإن له بيع أحد الكبيرين لأن العلة ما هو مظنة الضياع والاستيحاش وقد بقي له من يقوم مقام الثالث. وفي الكفاية : اجتمع له عدد من أقاربه لا يفرق بينه وبين واحد إن اختلفت جهة القرابة كالعم والخال أو اتحدت كخالين عند أبي يوسف لأنه يتوحش بفراق الكل والصحيح في المذهب أنه إذا كان الصغير أبواه لا أم وأخ أو أم وعمة أو خالة واحداً منهم، ولو كان معه يبيع أو أخ جاز بيع من سوى الأم لأن شفقة الأم تغني عمن سواها ولذا كانت أحق بالحضانة من غيرها، فهذه الصورة مستثناة من اختلاف الجهة. والجدة كالأم فلو كان معه جدة وعمة العمة والخالة، ولو كان معه عمة وخالة لا يباعوا إلا معاً لاختلاف الجهة مع اتحاد الدرجة. ولو كان معه أخوان أو إخوة كبار فالصحيح أنه يجوز بيع ما سوى واحد منهم الاستحسان لأن الشفقة أمر باطن لا يوقف عليه فيعتبر السبب ولا يعتبر الأبعد الأقرب وعند الاتحاد من الجهة والدرجة أحدهما يغني. وكذا لو ملك ستة إخوة ثلاثة كباراً وثلاثة صغاراً فباع من كل صغير كبيراً جاز ،استحساناً، فلو كان معه أخت شقيقة وأخت لأب وأخت لأم باع غير الشقيقة، ولو ادعاء رجلان فصار أبوين له ثم ملكوا جملة القياس أن يباع أحدهما لاتحاد جهتهما. وفي الاستحسان لا يباع لأن الأب في الحقيقة واحد فاحتمل كونه الذي بيع فيمتنع احتياطاً فصار الأصل أنه إذا كان معه عدد أحدهم أبعد جاز بيعه. وإن كانوا في درجة فإن كانوا من جنسين مختلفين كالأب والأم والخالة والعمة لا يفرق ولكن يباع الكل أو يمسك الكل، وإن كانوا من جنس واحد كالأخوين والعمين والخالين جاز أن الصغير أحدهما مع ويبيع ما سواه، ومثل الخالة والعمة أخ لأب وأخ لأم؛ كذا في فتح القدير. وكذا لا يرد عليه ما إذا كان البائع حربياً مستأمناً لمسلم فإنه لا يمنع المسلم من الشراء دفعاً للمفسدة عنه، وكذا لا يرد ما إذا باعه ممن حلف بعتقه إن اشتراه أو ملكه لما ذكرنا في الإعتاق. فهذه عشرة مسائل يجوز فيها التفريق ولا بأس بسردها: دفع أحدهما بجناية وبيعه بدين ورده بعيب وإذا كان المالك كافراً وإعتاقه وتدبيره واستيلادها وكتابته وبيعه ممن حلف بعتقه وبيع واحد من ثلاثة بالشرط السابق والحادية عشر إذا كان الصغير ورضيت أمه ببيعه فإنه يجوز كما في فتح القدير ولو كان مع امرأة مسبية صبي مراهق ادعت بعضهم من بعض والذي رأيته في الفتح يرزق بعضهم من بعض» بدون لفظ الجلالة. وفي حاشية الرملي عن ابن حجر الهيتمي وقع لشارح أنه زاد في غفلاتهم ونسبه المسلم وهو . غلط لا وجود لهذه الزيادة في مسلم بل ولا في كتب الحديث كما قضى به سبر ما بأيدي الناس منها اهـ. قوله : (ورضيت أمه ببيعه) عبارة الفتح : لو كان الولد مراهقاً فرضي بالبيع واختاره ورضيته أمه جاز بيعه .
His statement: (And he does not separate between a young child and a close mahram relative of his) because of his saying, peace be upon him: 'Whoever separates between a mother and her child, Allah will separate between him and his loved ones on the Day of Resurrection.' And the Prophet ﷺ gave to Ali two young slave boys who were brothers, then said to him: 'What did you do with the two boys?' He said: 'I sold one of them.' He said: 'Adrik adrik' and it is narrated 'Ardid ardid.' And because the young child takes comfort with the young and the adult, and the adult takes care of him. So in selling one of them is cutting off the comfort and preventing the care, and it is abandoning mercy upon the young, and the Prophet ﷺ has promised punishment. Then the prohibition is conditioned by the marital prohibition lineage, so that it does not include a non-related mahram nor a relative who is not mahram. Therefore, it is restricted to 'dhi rahim mahram', meaning a mahram by lineage. Otherwise, it would apply to the cousin if he is a brother through breastfeeding, for he is a mahram by lineage but does not have this ruling. He applied it generally, so it includes both young and old, and it is necessary that both be in his ownership. So if one of them belongs to him and the other to someone else, there is no harm in selling one. The author should have said 'except when the separation is by a valid right', because then separation is permissible, such as payment for a crime, or sale for a debt, or return due to a defect, because the consideration is to remove harm from others, not to harm him; as in al-Hidayah. And among separation by right is what is in al-Mabsut: a dhimmi has a slave who has a wife who is a slave woman and she gave birth to his child, then the slave becomes Muslim and his son is young; then the dhimmi is forced to sell the slave and his son, even if it separates him from his mother. It does not apply to the author's case of separation through emancipating one of them by wealth or otherwise, or tadbir, or istilad of the slave woman, or kitabah of one of them, for that is permissible because his intent is to prevent separation through sale, gift, bequest, or other causes of ownership, as in al-Jawharah, because if he were prevented from all that, the owner would be restricted from using his property entirely. Similarly, it does not apply if he owns three, one of them young, for he may sell one of the two adults, because the cause is the likelihood of loss and desolation, and there remains one to take the place of the third. In al-Kifayah: If he has a number of his relatives, he should not separate between him and even one if the kinship lines differ, like uncle and maternal uncle, or if they are the same like two maternal uncles according to Abu Yusuf, because he would be desolated by the separation of all. The correct in the madhhab is that if the child has no mother but a brother, or a mother and an aunt or maternal uncle, one of them, then it is permissible to sell other than the mother, because the mother's compassion suffices over others, and therefore she is more entitled to custody than others. This case is excepted from the difference of lineage. The grandmother is like the mother, so if he has a grandmother and a paternal aunt, the aunt and maternal uncle, and if he has a paternal aunt and maternal uncle, they cannot be sold except together due to differing lineage with equal degree. If he has two brothers or adult siblings, the correct is that it is permissible to sell all except one of them by istihsan, because compassion is an internal matter not known, so the cause is considered, and the closer is not considered over the farther. When the lineage and degree are the same, one suffices. Similarly, if he owns six brothers, three adults and three young, and he sells from each young one adult, it is permissible by istihsan. So if he has a full sister, a half-sister from father, and a half-sister from mother, he sells other than the full sister. If two men claim him as their son and become his fathers, then they own collectively, by analogy one may be sold due to unity of lineage, but by istihsan he is not sold because the father is essentially one, so it is possible that the one sold is the father, so it is prohibited out of caution. So the principle is that if he has a number where one is farther, it is permissible to sell him. If they are in the same degree, and if they are of different genders like father and mother, maternal uncle and paternal aunt, they are not separated but all are sold or all kept. If they are of the same gender like two brothers, two paternal uncles, two maternal uncles, it is permissible that the young one be with one and sell the rest. Similar to the maternal uncle and paternal aunt is a brother from father and a brother from mother; as in Fath al-Qadir. Similarly, it does not apply if the seller is a harbi musta'min for a Muslim, for he does not prevent the Muslim from buying to remove harm from him. Similarly, it does not apply if he sells it to someone who has sworn to free it if he buys or owns it, as mentioned in emancipation. These are ten issues where separation is permissible, and there is no harm in listing them: payment of one for a crime, sale for a debt, return due to a defect, if the owner is an infidel, emancipation, tadbir, istilad, kitabah, sale to one who swore to free it, sale of one out of three with the previous condition. And the eleventh is if the child is adolescent and his mother agrees to his sale, then it is permissible as in Fath al-Qadir. And if a captured woman has a young boy with her, he is adolescent, she claims [something]. What I saw in al-Fath is 'yurzuqu ba'dahum min ba'd' without the word of majesty. In the hashiah of al-Ramli from Ibn Hajar al-Haytami: The commentator made a mistake in their negligence and attributed it to Muslim, but it is an error; this addition does not exist in Muslim nor in any hadith books as verified by checking what is in people's hands. His statement: (And his mother agreed to his sale) The expression of al-Fath: If the child is adolescent and he is pleased with the sale and chooses it and his mother agrees to it, his sale is permissible.
Source pages p. 165

Commentary
This is a detailed commentary on the ruling that it is prohibited to separate a young child from a mahram relative through sale. The primary proof is the hadith: 'Whoever separates between a mother and her child, Allah will separate between him and his loved ones on the Day of Resurrection.' The prohibition also covers other mahram relatives, not just the mother. The reason is the child's need for companionship and care. The prohibition applies only when both the child and the relative are owned by the same person. If they have different owners, it is permissible to sell one. There are many exceptions where separation is permitted due to a valid right, such as when one of them is sold to pay a debt, or in case of crime compensation, or if the owner is a non-Muslim being forced to sell to a Muslim. The commentary lists ten specific situations where separation is allowed, and an eleventh from Fath al-Qadir when the child is adolescent and agrees with his mother's consent. The discussion includes many details about kinship types and degrees, based on istihsan and analogy. For example, if there are multiple relatives, the ruling changes based on closeness and relationship.

Key Terms
ذو رحم محرم (dhu rahim mahram): A relative with whom marriage is permanently prohibited due to blood relationship (nasab).
تفريق (tafriq): The act of separating a child from a mahram relative through a sale or other transfer of ownership.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference used to relax the strict analogy (qiyas) for a more equitable ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In which of the following situations is it permissible to separate a child from a mahram relative?
A) Sale to pay a debt.
B) Emancipation of one of them.
C) Both A and B.
D) Neither.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prohibits separating a child from a mahram relative through sale, but allows it for valid rights and by istihsan in many cases.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
10 min
The Ruling on Separating a Minor from Relatives in Sale
Rules on separating a minor from relatives in sale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on separating a minor from relatives in a sale, identify the exceptions for mother and grandmother, and apply the principles to different kinship combinations.

Core Idea
A minor must retain at least one caring relative; selling all is makruh tahrimi but the sale is valid.

In classical Hanafi fiqh, the sale of a minor's relatives is permitted as long as the minor is not left without a caring relative. This lesson unpacks the detailed rules from Al-Bahr al-Raiq, covering when it is permissible to sell some relatives and when it is prohibited. The mother and grandmother are never separated because their compassion is deemed sufficient.

Guided Path
1
Identify the General Rule
Understand that a minor should not be left without any caring relative. The default is that separation is permissible if at least one suitable relative remains with the minor.
The rule is based on istihsan, prioritizing the minor's welfare over strict qiyas.
2
Analyze Kinship Types and Degrees
Distinguish between relatives of different types (e.g., paternal uncle and maternal uncle) and same type (e.g., two maternal uncles). If types differ, one must be kept. If type and degree are same, one suffices.
Abu Yusuf’s stricter view requires keeping one even if same type, but the mufta bihi follows Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.
3
Apply the Mother/Grandmother Exception
The mother and grandmother are exceptions; they can never be sold. Their compassion is unique, so even if other relatives are present, the mother stays.
This is derived from her right to custody (hadana).
4
Examine the List of Permissible Separations
Review the ten (or eleven) scenarios where separation is allowed without restriction, such as selling to pay a debt or returning a defective item.
These are specific concessions; the general prohibition on total separation remains.
5
Consider the Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Note the difference between Abu Yusuf and the majority: Abu Yusuf prohibits selling all relatives of the same type, while the majority allows it. The mufta bihi is the majority view.
This difference affects practical cases like selling one of two maternal uncles.

And if he has with him a father or brother, it is permissible to sell other than the mother because the compassion of the mother suffices beyond others, and thus she is more entitled to custody than others. This case is exempted from the difference in type. And the grandmother is like the mother, so if he has with him a grandmother and a paternal aunt, the paternal aunt and maternal aunt [can be sold?]. And if he has with him a paternal aunt and a maternal aunt, they are not sold except together because of the difference in type with unity of degree. Likewise, if he owns six brothers, three adults and three minors, and he sells from each minor an adult, it is permissible by istihsan. By istihsan he is not sold because the father in reality is one, so it is possible that he is the one sold, so it is prohibited out of precaution. So the principle is: if he has with him a number, one of whom is more distant, it is permissible to sell him. And if they are of the same degree, if they are of two different types like father and mother and maternal aunt and paternal aunt, they are not separated, but all are sold or all are retained. Because he is not her son, lineage is not established, and they are not separated as a precaution. And if he sells the mother with a stipulation of option, then buys the child, executing the sale is disliked because they come together in his ownership. And if a minor is in his possession and he buys his mother with a stipulation of option, he may return her by agreement (the ownership is with him and to repel harm from him according to them). And it is authentic that he separated between Mariya and Sirin and they were two adult sisters. And the married couple is not included because the text came contrary to analogy, so it is confined to its subject. If he separates in a prohibited place, it is disliked but the contract is valid. From Abu Yusuf: it is not permissible in blood kinship and is permissible in other than that. From him also: it is not permissible in all because the command to cancel and return is only in an invalid sale. And for them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad): the pillar of sale came from its appropriate party, and the dislike is due to an adjacent meaning, so it resembles the dislike of offering a price while another is negotiating. And in al-Jawhara: everything that is disliked of separation in sale is disliked in division in inheritance and spoils. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 166

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq, a commentary on Kanz al-Daqaiq, addresses the ruling on separating a minor from his relatives when selling them. The core principle is that a minor should not be left without any compassionate relative because that would cause him harm. Thus, if a minor has multiple relatives, it is permissible to sell some as long as at least one remains who can care for him. The text details various scenarios based on the type and degree of kinship. If the relatives are of different types (e.g., paternal uncle and maternal uncle), one must be kept. If they are of the same type (e.g., two maternal uncles), Abu Yusuf holds that one must be kept to prevent desolation, but the correct position is that it is permissible to sell all but one. Special exceptions are made for the mother and grandmother, whose compassion is deemed sufficient, so they are never separated from the minor. The text also lists ten situations where separation is allowed, such as selling to pay a debt or returning a defective item. Finally, it notes a difference of opinion: Abu Yusuf restricts the prohibition to blood relatives, while others extend it to all, but the relied-upon view is that the prohibition is limited to the cases mentioned in the hadith.

Key Terms
استحسان (istihsan): A method of legal reasoning that prefers a ruling based on convenience or equity over strict analogy (qiyas), used here to allow selling some relatives.
الشفقة (al-shafaqa): Compassion or care, particularly of a mother or close relative, which is considered sufficient to prevent harm to the minor.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A minor has with him his mother and a paternal uncle. According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on selling the paternal uncle?
A) It is not permissible because the mother alone is not sufficient.
B) It is permissible because the mother's compassion suffices, so the uncle can be sold.
C) It is only permissible if the uncle consents.
D) It is impermissible because both must stay with the minor.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a minor must retain at least one caring relative; the mother and grandmother can never be sold away.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

The Definition and Types of Rescission (Iqala) in Sale
Defines rescission linguistically and legally, outlines ten aspects of its ruling.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the linguistic and legal definitions of rescission (iqala) in the Hanafi school and identify the three categories of sale to which rescission applies.

Core Idea
Rescission lifts the contract, not the sale — it applies by mutual consent to valid sales and forcibly to invalid ones.

In this lesson, we explore the foundational definition of rescission (iqala) in the Hanafi school. The author of al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies that rescission is not merely cancellation but a lifting of the contract, and it applies across all types of sales — valid, disliked, and invalid. We will examine the linguistic roots, the legal meaning, and the key distinction between rescission by mutual consent and forced rescission.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scope of rescission
Determine which types of contracts rescission covers: all sale contracts, whether valid, disliked, or invalid.
Rescission is not limited to invalid contracts.
2
Distinguish between two modes of rescission
For valid and disliked sales, rescission is by mutual consent. For invalid or prohibitively disliked sales, rescission is obligatory and forcible (without mutual consent).
The text states: 'وإن كان واجباً في المكروه تحريماً دافعاً للمعصية أو فاسداً فيفسخ بدون التراضي'.
3
Analyze the ten topics outlined
The author lists ten aspects of rescission: linguistic meaning, legal meaning, pillar, conditions, nature, ruling, who can rescind, evidence, cause, and benefits. This structures the full discussion.
These ten topics are enumerated in the passage.
4
Examine the linguistic etymology
According to al-Qamus and al-Misbah, 'iqala' is derived from 'qayl' (lifting/removing), not 'qawl' (speech). The hamza indicates negation: removing the first statement.
This refutes a common misconception that it comes from 'qawl'.
5
Formulate the legal definition
Legally, rescission is defined as lifting the contract (رفع العقد). For sale specifically, it is the lifting of a sale contract.
This definition is general; divorce is a different type of lifting.

Source Text

باب الإقالة المناسبة ظاهرة وهي شاملة لكل عقد بيع صحيحاً كان أو مكروهاً فيفسخ إقالة بالتراضي وإن كان واجباً في المكروه تحريماً دافعاً للمعصية أو فاسداً فيفسخ بدون التراضي إما من أحدهما أو من القاضي جبراً كما قدمناه فاشترك المكروه والفاسد في وجوب الدفع. والكلام فيها يقع في عشرة مواضع: الأول في معناها لغة والثاني في معناها شرعاً. والثالث في ركنها والرابع في شروطها والخامس في صفتها والسادس في حكمها. والسابع فيمن يملكها ومن لا يملكها والثامن في بيان دليلها والتاسع في سببها. والعاشر في محاسنها. أما الأول فقال في القاموس : قلته البيع بالكسر وأقلته فسخته، واستقاله طلب إليه أن يقيله وتقايل البيعان وأقال الله عثرتك وأقالكها اهـ. ذكرها في القاف مع الياء. وفي المصباح : : أقال الله عثرته إذا رفعه من سقوطه ومنه الإقالة في البيع لأنها رفع العقد، وقاله قيلاً من باب باع لغة واستقاله البيع فأقاله .اهـ. وبهذا ظهر أنها لم تكن مشتقة من القول وأن الهمزة للسلب أي أزال القول الأول كما ذكره الشارح وإنما هي من القيل. وأما معناها شرعاً فهي رفع العقد؛ كذا ذكره في الجوهرة وهو تعريف للأعم من إقالة البيع والإجارة ونحوهما. وإن أردت خصوصها فقل رفع عقد البيع، وأما الطلاق فهو رفع قيد النكاح لا باب الإقالة قوله : (كما قدمناه) أي قبيل قول المصنف إلا أن يبيع المشتري . قوله : (وأما حكمها فاختلف
Chapter of Rescission. The connection is apparent, and it includes every contract of sale, whether valid or disliked, so it is rescinded by mutual consent as rescission. And if it is obligatory in the disliked (prohibitively) to repel sin, or if it is invalid, it is rescinded without mutual consent, either by one of them or by the judge forcibly, as we have presented. So the disliked and the invalid share the obligation of annulment. The discussion on it falls into ten topics: first, its linguistic meaning; second, its legal meaning; third, its pillar; fourth, its conditions; fifth, its nature; sixth, its ruling; seventh, who has the right to rescind and who does not; eighth, its evidence; ninth, its cause; tenth, its benefits. As for the first, al-Qamus said: 'I rescinded the sale' (with kasra) and 'I granted rescission' meaning I annulled it. 'He asked for rescission' meaning he requested that he rescind. 'The two parties rescinded mutually.' And 'May Allah rescind your stumble and grant you rescission from it.' He mentioned it in the letter qaf with ya. In al-Misbah: 'Allah rescinded his stumble' if He lifted him from his fall. From this comes rescission in sale because it is the lifting of the contract. And 'he spoke' from the paradigm of 'ba'a'. 'He asked him to rescind the sale and he rescinded.' Thus it is clear that it is not derived from 'qawl' (speech) and that the hamza is for negation, meaning he removed the first statement, as the commentator mentioned, but rather it is from 'qayl'. As for its legal meaning, it is the lifting of the contract; thus mentioned in al-Jawhara, and it is a definition general to rescission of sale, lease, and the like. If you want its specific definition, say: lifting of a sale contract. As for divorce, it is the lifting of the marriage tie, not rescission. Qawluh: (as we have presented) i.e., before the author's statement 'unless the buyer sells' Qawluh: (and as for its ruling, it is differed)
Source pages p. 167

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq introduces the chapter on rescission (iqala) in sale. The author first explains that rescission applies to all types of sales: valid (صحيح), disliked (مكروه), and invalid (فاسد). For valid and disliked sales, rescission occurs by mutual consent; for invalid sales, it must be done forcibly without consent. The passage then outlines ten topics that will be discussed: linguistic meaning, legal meaning, pillar, conditions, nature, ruling, who can rescind, evidence, cause, and benefits. The commentator then provides the linguistic definition from al-Qamus and al-Misbah, showing that 'iqala' comes from the root 'qayl' meaning to lift or remove, not from 'qawl' (speech). Legally, it is defined as lifting the contract, which includes rescission of sale, lease, etc. The specific definition for sale is 'lifting of a sale contract'. The passage ends with a note clarifying that divorce is not rescission but rather lifting the marriage tie. This sets the foundation for the detailed discussions to follow.

Key Terms
الإقالة (al-iqala): Rescission or annulment of a contract, particularly a sale, by mutual consent or forcibly in case of invalid contracts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the legal definition of rescission (iqala) in the context of sale?
A) The cancellation of a sale due to a defect.
B) The lifting of the contract of sale.
C) The renewal of the contract with new terms.
D) The termination of ownership without consent.

Key Takeaway
Rescission (iqala) is the lifting of a sale contract, applicable to valid, disliked, and invalid sales, with mutual consent for valid/disliked and forcible annulment for invalid/prohibitively disliked.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
beginner
8 min
The Definition and Pillar of Iqalah (Rescission of Sale)
Defines iqalah linguistically and legally, and explains its pillar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the linguistic and legal definitions of iqalah and explain the Hanafi dispute regarding the verbal form of its pillar.

Core Idea
Iqalah is a rescission (raf‘ al-‘aqd), not a new sale, and its pillar requires mutual offer and acceptance.

The chapter on iqalah begins by clarifying what iqalah means—both in language and in law. The passage distinguishes iqalah from divorce and from a new sale, and then explains that its essential component (rukn) is offer and acceptance. However, within the Hanafi school there is a difference of opinion on whether both parties must use past tense verbs or if a combination of future and past suffices. Understanding this definition and the disagreement forms the basis for applying the rules of rescission.

Guided Path
1
Identify the linguistic derivation
Read the linguistic discussion: iqalah comes from 'qayl' (to lift), not 'qawl' (speech). The hamza is for removal, so iqalah means 'removing the previous statement'.
The author quotes al-Qamus and al-Misbah to confirm this origin.
2
Grasp the legal definition
Find the legal definition: 'raf‘ al-‘aqd' (lifting the contract). Note that this is general for all contracts, but for sale it is specifically 'raf‘ ‘aqd al-bay‘'. Distinguish it from divorce, which lifts the restriction of marriage, not the marriage itself.
The text also notes the ten topics to be covered; this lesson focuses on the first three.
3
Examine the pillar (rukn)
The pillar is offer and acceptance. The text lists valid verbal forms: two past tense verbs, or one future/imperative and one past. It also mentions acceptance by action (cutting the item) and valid terms like 'faskhtu' or 'taraktu'.
Pay attention to the phrase 'wa tan‘aqidu bi al-ta‘āti'—it can also be concluded by mutual handing over.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf allow a future verb (e.g., 'aqilni') followed by a past verb ('aqaltuka'), likening it to marriage. Muhammad requires both in past tense, likening iqalah to sale. The text says 'wa huwa al-sahih' (and that is the correct view), likely siding with Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf.
This dispute affects validity: if one party uses a future tense, Muhammad would deem the iqalah invalid, while the other two imams would validate it.

Source Text

باب الإقالة . محله المناسبة ظاهرة وهي شاملة لكل عقد بيع صحيحاً كان أو مكروهاً فيفسخ إقالة بالتراضي وإن كان واجباً في المكروه تحريماً دافعاً للمعصية أو فاسداً فيفسخ بدون التراضي إما من أحدهما أو من القاضي جبراً كما قدمناه فاشترك المكروه والفاسد في وجوب الدفع. والكلام فيها يقع في عشرة مواضع: الأول في معناها لغة والثاني في معناها شرعاً. والثالث في ركنها والرابع في شروطها والخامس في صفتها والسادس في حكمها. والسابع فيمن يملكها ومن لا يملكها والثامن في بيان دليلها والتاسع في سببها. والعاشر في محاسنها. أما الأول فقال في القاموس : قلته البيع بالكسر وأقلته فسخته، واستقاله طلب إليه أن يقيله وتقايل البيعان وأقال الله عثرتك وأقالكها اهـ. ذكرها في القاف مع الياء. وفي المصباح : : أقال الله عثرته إذا رفعه من سقوطه ومنه الإقالة في البيع لأنها رفع العقد، وقاله قيلاً من باب باع لغة واستقاله البيع فأقاله .اهـ. وبهذا ظهر أنها لم تكن مشتقة من القول وأن الهمزة للسلب أي أزال القول الأول كما ذكره الشارح وإنما هي من القيل. وأما معناها شرعاً فهي رفع العقد؛ كذا ذكره في الجوهرة وهو تعريف للأعم من إقالة البيع والإجارة ونحوهما. وإن أردت خصوصها فقل رفع عقد البيع، وأما الطلاق فهو رفع قيد النكاح لا رفع النكاح. وأما ركنها فالإيجاب والقبول الدالان عليها بلفظين ماضيين أو أحدهما مستقبلاً والآخر ماضياً كاقلني فقال أقلتك عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف كالنكاح. وقال محمد : لا تنقعد إلا بماضيين كالبيع ؛ كذا في البدائع. وقد يكون القبول بالفعل كما لو قطعه قميصاً في فور قول المشتري أقلتك، وتنعقد بفاسختك وتركت وتاركتك ودفعت وتنعقد بالتعاطي كالبيع كما في الخانية والخلاصة. وفي البزازية ينعقد به كالبيع من أحد الجانبين وهو الصحيح.
Chapter of Iqalah. Its place: the appropriateness is apparent, and it includes every sale contract, valid or disliked; then it is rescinded by iqalah with mutual consent, and if it is wajib in the makruh tahrimi to prevent sin, or if it is fasid, then it is rescinded without mutual consent, either by one of them or by the judge forcibly as we have presented. So the makruh and fasid share the obligation of cancellation. And discussion about it occurs in ten topics: first, its linguistic meaning; second, its legal meaning; third, its pillar; fourth, its conditions; fifth, its description; sixth, its ruling; seventh, who has the right to perform it and who does not; eighth, its evidence; ninth, its cause; tenth, its virtues. As for the first, al-Qamus said: 'Qaltu al-bay'a bi al-kasr, aqaltuhu faskhatuhu, istaqalahu talaba ilayhi an yuqilahu, taqayala al-bay'an, aqala Allahu athrata wa aqalakaha' end quote. He mentioned it in the letter qaf with ya. And in al-Misbah: 'Aqala Allahu athratahu idha rafa'ahu min suqutihi, minhu al-iqalah fi al-bay'i li annaha raf' al-aqd; wa qalahu qaylan min bab ba'a lughatan, wastaqalahu al-bay'a fa aqalahu' end quote. By this it appears that it is not derived from qawl, and that the hamza is for removal, i.e., removed the first statement as the commentator mentioned; rather it is from qayl. As for its legal meaning, it is the lifting of the contract; thus it was mentioned in al-Jawharah, and it is a definition for the general, including iqalah of sale, lease, and similar. If you want its specific, say: lifting of the sale contract; as for divorce, it is lifting the restriction of marriage, not lifting the marriage itself. As for its pillar: it is the offer and acceptance that indicate it with two past tense verbs, or one future and the other past, like if the buyer says 'Aqilni' and the seller says 'Aqaltuka' according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, like marriage. Muhammad said: it is only concluded with two past tense verbs, like sale; thus in al-Bada'i. And acceptance may be by action, as if he cuts it into a shirt immediately upon the buyer's saying 'I release you,' and it is concluded by 'I rescind,' 'I leave,' 'I abandon you,' 'I return,' and it is concluded by mutual giving (ta'ati) like sale, as in al-Khaniyah and al-Khulasah. In al-Bazzaziyyah, it is concluded by it like sale from one side, and that is the correct view.
Source pages p. 167

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on iqalah (rescission of sale) by first outlining ten topics to be discussed. The author then delves into the first two: linguistic and legal meanings. Linguistically, iqalah is derived from the root 'q-y-l' meaning to lift or remove, not from 'q-w-l' (speech). The hamza is for removal, i.e., removing the previous statement. Legally, iqalah is defined as the lifting of a contract; this is a general definition that covers iqalah in sales, leases, etc. Specifically for sales, it is lifting the sale contract. The author distinguishes it from divorce, which lifts the restriction of marriage, not the marriage itself. Then the pillar (rukn) is discussed: it consists of offer and acceptance. There is an intra-Hanafi difference on the linguistic form: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf accept a combination of future and past tense verbs (e.g., buyer says 'Aqilni' [imperative] and seller says 'Aqaltuka' [past]), similar to marriage. According to Muhammad, only past tense verbs are valid, as in sale. The passage also notes that acceptance can be by action, and that terms like 'I rescind,' 'I leave,' etc., are valid. Mutual giving (ta'ati) is also valid. This shows that iqalah is flexible in form but must indicate mutual agreement.

Key Terms
الإقالة (al-iqalah): Lifting the contract; rescinding a sale by mutual agreement.
الركن (al-rukn): The essential component of iqalah: offer and acceptance.
التعاطي (al-ta‘āti): Mutual handing over (exchange without spoken words); recognized as a valid method for concluding iqalah.
الفسخ (al-faskh): Rescission; annulment of a contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the legal definition of iqalah?
A) A new sale with mutual consent
B) The lifting of the contract (raf‘ al-‘aqd)
C) The lifting of the marriage bond
D) A gift or charity

Key Takeaway
Iqalah is a rescission (raf‘ al-‘aqd) by mutual agreement, and its pillar is offer and acceptance, with a valid difference on whether future tense verbs suffice.
